### 3 Recognition Program Design

|   |   |   |   |   | Group A |   |   | Group B |   |   |

| 3.1 | Please benchmark Wells Fargo’s global recognition program against industry peers and best in class global recognition programs.  Please describe the benchmarking methodology and data sources you use. | Vantage Circle will partner with Mercer as a subcontractor to provide independent benchmarking data. Mercer employs a comprehensive benchmarking methodology that integrates proprietary global recognition survey data, client-specific program metrics, and external market research to provide a robust comparison against industry peers and insights into the latest trends and capabilities of leading global recognition programs. Mercer's 2025 Employee Recognition Survey is a comprehensive and independent data set on recognition practices across more than 1000 organizations globally, representing 15+ industries. The majority of survey respondents consist of global organizations with an annual revenue over $1B, representing the organizational complexity against which Wells Fargo should benchmark its program design. Mercer’s recognition survey data covers reward redemption patterns, program design features, monetary and non-monetary awards, program budgets, and more. Data normalization techniques are applied to account for differences in company size, industry sector, and geographic footprint, ensuring that benchmarking insights are relevant and contextualized for each client. In addition to Mercer's 2025 Employee Recognition Survey, program benchmarking consists of external research into best practices, and qualitative findings from past client engagements. Moreover, Mercer's Global Talent Trends provides valuable insights on global employee preferences and shifting total rewards practices. By combining quantitative data with qualitative assessments, Mercer can deliver a holistic view of Wells Fargo's recognition program performance relative to global standards.  Additionally, Vantage Circle provides recognition program benchmarks using our proprietary AIRe Framework - the only behavioural science grounded, globally validated, quantitative methodology for assessing R&R program design. AIRe is grounded in behavioural science and evaluates programs across four drivers (Appreciation, Incentivization, Reinforcement, eMotional Connect) and two meta-drivers (Authenticity and Impact). We have provided a detailed understanding of our point of view on Recognitition and the AIRe framework in the attachment: Vantage Circle POV and Framework (slides 2 -14)  Our benchmarking draws on three data sources: 1. AIRe Global Assessment Database: Since launching in 2022, over 2,000 organizations worldwide have completed the AIRe assessment, making it the largest comparative dataset on recognition program design and effectiveness. 2. Annual Global + Country Reports: We publish the industry’s only AIRe-based recognition reports—global editions in 2022 and 2025, plus country-specific benchmarks for the US, UK, India, and UAE across 2023–2024. These provide peer comparisons by industry, size, maturity, and geography. 3. Program Design Reviews & Client Studies: We continuously analyze best-in-class programs across large global enterprises, translating insights into design principles, usage patterns, ROI/ROE drivers, and cultural impact indicators. 4. Recognition scorecard with Great Place to Work (GPTW) India: We also partner with GPTW to run an annual Recognition Landscape Report and deliver customised Recognition Scorecard Reports for clients which ananlyse both Voice of Employees and Recognition Program Design to surface if employees are feeling recognised (and the business impact of feeling recognised versus not feeling recognised) vis. the program design and opportunities for enhancement.  Our benchmarking approach for Wells Fargo includes: - Mapping each program component (eCards, manager awards, milestones, retirement recognition) to the AIRe dimensions - Assessing strengths, blind spots, and cultural alignment - Comparing results against global peers in financial services and large multi-country organizations - Identifying design gaps and opportunities based on behavioural-science-led patterns observed across our benchmark base This methodology ensures Wells Fargo is evaluated not just against peers, but against the highest-performing recognition cultures globally. You can check out our AIRe assessment here - https://www.vantagecircle.com/tools/AIRe-score-assessment/  While we were unable to do a full-blown AIRe assessment of program design based on the provided summary of the current program, here is a 1st level benchmarking assessment, wherein we have compared your program to global BFSI companies reporting high program effectiveness ("Leaders").   Wells Fargo vs Global BFSI Benchmarks  1. Coverage & Scale: With 235k employees eCards: 1.5M+ annually → ~6.4 eCards per employee per year, indicating high usage frequency. Service milestones: 80,000 annually → 34% of workforce recognized each year for tenure alone. New hire recognition: 40,000 annually → Reflects consistent onboarding coverage. Retirements: ~1,000 annually.  Benchmark comparison: BFSI Leaders show varied coverage, with only 5% achieving 80%+ annual recognition coverage and only 14% reaching 60–79%. With your volumes, Wells Fargo likely sits in the upper tiers of coverage, though exact % of employees receiving any recognition (eCard or award) would confirm this.  Strength: High participation & broad reach. Gap: Need verified unique employee coverage % to benchmark precisely  2. Award Types vs BFSI Leader Mix BFSI Leaders most commonly offer: Onboarding (68%), Long Service (95%), Peer recognition (86%), Spot Awards (77%), Recurring awards (Monthly 50%, Quarterly 68%, Annual 77%).  Wells Fargo alignment: ✔ Onboarding gift boxes ✔ Peer eCards (high volume) ✔ Manager monetary awards ✔ Long service & retirement recognition  Gaps vs leaders No explicit monthly/quarterly/annual awards. No mention of special project awards. Occasions (birthdays, etc.) are not formalized as a distinct programmed stream.  3. Reward Types vs BFSI Leader Practices: BFSI Leaders frequently use Points/gift catalogue (64%), Swag (41%), Mementos (86%) Wells Fargo matches all of these well.  Gaps vs leaders Learning rewards (36% leaders) – not mentioned. Leader interactions (36% leaders) – not used as an award type. Experiential rewards (18%) – not currently offered. These are common “impact amplifiers” among BFSI leaders.  4. Execution & Communication  BFSI leaders outperform others by using - Regular communications (64%) - Marketing campaigns (82%) - Success story sharing (45%) - Ambassadors/champions (36%) - Gamification (27%)  Wells Fargo strengths ✔ Real-time and scheduled delivery ✔ Global fulfillment for physical gifts ✔ CEO touchpoints for milestones  Gaps vs leaders  No stated use of structured campaigns, internal champions, gamification, or success stories. No mention of social feeds, town-hall amplification, or structured award events, all of which are widely used by BFSI leaders. These are major differentiators between leaders and others.  5. Behavioral & ROI Practices:  BFSI Leaders emphasize - Behavior-linked criteria (45% balance results + behaviors) - Mechanisms for consistency (59% use escalating rewards/badges) - ROI tracking (95%) Wells Fargo: You link recognition to accomplishment scope, but no mention of behavioral framing, badges/titles, or ROI tracking. These are significant maturity markers among BFSI leaders.  Summary: Strengths & Priority Gaps Wells Fargo Recognition Strengths - High-frequency global peer recognition (1.5M eCards for 235k employees). - Comprehensive lifecycle coverage (joiners, service awards, retirement). - Strong symbolic + choice-based rewards (points catalogue, certificates, commemoratives). - Robust global fulfillment operations.  Key Improvement Opportunities (vs BFSI Leaders) 1. Introduce structured recurring awards (monthly/quarterly/annual + strategic project awards). 2. Formalize special-occasion recognition (birthdays, personal celebrations) as a defined stream. 3. Add learning, experiential, and leader-interaction reward types. 4. Expand program storytelling, marketing, champions, and gamification. 5. Increase visibility via social feeds, events, and leadership personalization. 6. Implement behavior-linked tiers, badges, and formal ROI tracking |  | Benchmarking: Saurabh |  |  |  | I added Mercer's benchmarking at the top of this answer and modified the first sentence of Saurabh's answer so that it would flow. |  |  |
| 3.2 | Please benchmark Wells Fargo’s global recognition program against industry peers and best in class global recognition programs.  Please describe the types of metrics and comparisons available. | Vantage Circle will partner with Mercer as a subcontractor to provide independent benchmarking data. Mercer will benchmark Wells Fargo's recognition program using a balanced set of quantitative and qualitative metrics. Quantitative metrics include participation rates, frequency of recognition events, reward redemption rates, employee engagement scores, and program ROI indicators. Qualitative comparisons assess program communication effectiveness, platform usability, and alignment with organizational culture. These metrics are compared across industry peers, similarly sized organizations, geographic regions, and program maturity levels. Mercer’s approach also incorporates best-in-class global program benchmarks to identify innovation trends and leading practices, enabling clients to understand their relative position and opportunities for advancement.  Additionally, Vantage Circle's the AIRe assessment provides structured design and execution metrics aligned to the four AIRe drivers (Appreciation, Incentivization, Reinforcement, eMotional Connect) and the meta-drivers of Authenticity and Impact.   Design metrics include: - Coverage of recognition moments (onboarding, milestones, appreciations, spot awards, monthly/quarterly/annual awards, special awards) across employee segments - Criteria for award determination (results vs behaviours) - Approach to team vs individual recognition - Mechanisms to reinforce consistency (escalating awards, exclusive badges/titles) - Recognition delivery channels (social feed, team meetings, events, leader messages) - Internal communication, documentation, training, and clarity of criteria - Reward mix (cash, points, catalogue, privileges, experiences, swag, learning, leadership interactions) - Perceived effectiveness across engagement, retention, performance, culture, and DE&I  Execution metrics (available for clients on the VC platform) include: - Unique login rate - Receiver and giver coverage (monetary and non-monetary) - Recognition mix (non-monetary vs monetary) - Average recognition moments per employee (weighted recognitions, comments, likes) - Average recognition post length (monetary and non-monetary) - Budget utilization - Reward redemption rate - Redemption category trends (gift cards vs merchandise)  Benchmarking availability: Benchmarks are available against global industry-specific and regional pan-industry cohorts. We also produce custom peer-group cuts tailored to organizations with global footprints similar to Wells Fargo.  In addition, the 2025 Global AIRe Report analyses what differentiates high-effectiveness programs from others, giving Wells Fargo visibility not only into what peers are doing, but what the most successful recognition cultures do differently in design, governance, and behavioural reinforcement.   You can test out our benchmarking insights custom GPT here - https://chatgpt.com/g/g-68fa43f4860081918d59b7a4c348dee2-vantage-recognition-insights-tool |  | Benchmarking: Saurabh |  |  |  | I added Mercer's benchmarking at the top of this answer and modified the first sentence of Saurabh's answer so that it would flow. |  |  |
| 3.3 | Please benchmark Wells Fargo’s global recognition program against industry peers and best in class global recognition programs.  Please describe how benchmarking insights are delivered and used to improve program outcomes. | Vantage Circle will partner with Mercer as a subcontractor to provide independent benchmarking data. Benchmarking insights are delivered through detailed, customized reports that highlight program strengths, gaps to market, and opportunities for improvement. Mercer can facilitate collaborative workshops with Wells Fargo stakeholders and the Vantage Circle project team to interpret these insights and co-create actionable plans. The insights inform refinements in program design, communication strategies, and reward offerings, driving enhanced employee engagement and program effectiveness. Prioritized recommendations based on impact and feasibility support continuous improvement cycles, enabling clients to adapt their recognition programs dynamically in response to evolving workforce needs and market trends.  Additionally, Vantage Circle benchmarking insights are delivered through a combination of self-service tools, advisory consultations, research-based reports, and structured program reviews—ensuring that insights directly influence program outcomes.  We start with the DIY AIRe Assessment Report, which gives an instant, quantitative view of design strengths and gaps. This is pAIRed with an on-demand consultation where our experts interpret results, compare against relevant benchmarks, and recommend targeted improvements.  We also provide access to the R&R Advisor (beta) — a self-service design evaluation AI tool that allows clients to run their own AIRe-based program assessments and receive automated, behaviourally grounded recommendations on how to strengthen appreciation, incentivization, reinforcement, and emotional connect.  These inputs are complemented by our annual Global AIRe Recognition Report, as well as on-demand benchmarking intelligence through the Insights GPT. Together, these resources help organizations understand not only peer norms but also what differentiates high-effectiveness programs globally.  Through our partnership with Great Place to Work® India, we offer an R&R Scorecard that integrates employee perception (feeling recognised, cultural impact, discretionary effort) with AIRe program design scores. This correlation highlights misalignments—such as strong structures but low felt recognition—and identifies which design elements have the greatest influence on business and cultural outcomes.  For key clients, benchmarking is embedded into ongoing governance. Beyond quarterly reviews, we conduct an Annual Recognition Program Audit that evaluates design maturity, highlights gaps, and recommends enhancements, including potential new features, design refinements, and configuration improvements.  Together, these mechanisms ensure benchmarking insights are not only shared but actively translated into improved usage, stronger cultural reinforcement, and measurable program impact. |  | Benchmarking: Saurabh |  |  |  | I added Mercer's benchmarking at the top of this answer and modified the first sentence of Saurabh's answer so that it would flow. |  |  |

These reports are complemented by executive summaries, trend analyses, gap analyses, and strategic recommendations.   Additionally, Vantag Circle provides clients with a range of benchmarking reports and analyses that translate AIRe insights into clear, actionable improvements. Examples include: - AIRe Assessment Report: A quantitative, design-focused benchmark showing how the client compares with global, regional, and industry peers across the AIRe drivers. - R&R Advisor (beta) Output: A self-service design assessment with automated recommendations and comparison against AIRe global norms. - Quarterly Business Review (QBR): A structured review of key metrics (adoption, coverage, mix, message quality, redemption trends, budget utilisation), where we identify gaps and opportunities and jointly plan enhancements, fixes, and configuration improvements. - Annual Recognition Program Audit: A deep-dive evaluation of design maturity, usage patterns, governance strength, and alignment to high-performing programs, with clear recommendations for improvement. - Global + Country AIRe Report Extracts: Insights from our 2025 Global Report and prior US/UK/India/UAE editions, highlighting practices that differentiate high-effectiveness programs. - GPTW–VC R&R Scorecard: A combined view of employee perception (“feeling recognised”) and AIRe program design benchmarks to identify misalignments between program structure and employee experience. - Insights GPT Snapshots: On-demand extracts showing peer practices, cross-industry trends, and design patterns from our global dataset.  These deliverables ensure clients receive both point-in-time benchmarks and continuous guidance to improve program effectiveness throughout the year. |  | Benchmarking: Saurabh |  |  |  | I added Mercer's benchmarking at the top of this answer and modified the first sentence of Saurabh's answer so that it would flow. |  |  |
| 3.5 | Please describe your approach to evaluating and transforming an existing recognition program to achieve best-in-class status. In your response, address the following:  Assessment of Current State: How will you review and assess our existing recognition program, platform features, and processes?  What methods will you use to identify strengths, gaps, and opportunities for improvement? | Vantage Circle will partner with Mercer as a subcontractor to provide program assessment services. Mercer will conduct a thorough program audit encompassing program design, platform capabilities, communication strategies, and governance structures. Platform features will be assessed by Vantage in comparison to our platform capabilties. This assessment includes employee listening and detailed review of market best practice to capture a comprehensive view of program performance. For an organization of Wells Fargo's size and complexity, Mercer recommends our asynchronous digital focus group tool, Remesh, which can include up to 1000 global participants per session, and uses customize questions and  based on participant responses. The tool supports both synchronous and asynchronous participation, multi-language conversations, and accommodates diverse audiences across time zones. Mercer will conduct up to 3 Remesh sessions (Americas, EMEA and ASIA zones). Using employee listening and market benchmarks, Mercer will apply a structured gap analysis framework and maturity model to evaluate current program sophistication and alignment with organizational goals.   Additionally, we will infuse our transformation approach which is anchored in the AIRᵉ Framework and combines behavioural-science evaluation, platform diagnostics, and stakeholder insights to redesign programs to best-in-class standards.  Assessment of Current State We begin with a comprehensive AIRᵉ Design Assessment to benchmark Wells Fargo’s existing program architecture (award types, criteria, coverage, behavioural alignment, communication, and consistency). In parallel, we conduct a structured platform features and functionality review, covering: • End-to-end platform workflows (nomination → approval → fulfilment), • Usability and accessibility across devices (especially critical for frontline and operations-site employees), • Social visibility and peer-to-peer mechanisms, • Catalogue and reward experience, • Reporting, insights, and manager dashboards, • Integration points with HRIS, PMS, LMS and internal collaboration tools, • Configurations that influence user behaviour (nudges, notifications, approvals, budgets), and • The overall user experience for employees, managers, HR admins and leaders. This feature-level diagnostic helps us understand what is working well, what is underutilised, and what may be creating friction or limiting participation.  We also review platform-level usage through adoption analytics (logins, recognitions, giver/receiver coverage, recognition mix, message quality, redemption patterns, and budget utilisation). In addition, we carry out a process and governance assessment across nomination workflows, manager enablement, communication, and fulfilment. Identifying Strengths, Gaps, and Opportunities Gaps and opportunities are identified through a combination of: • AIRᵉ benchmark comparisons (industry, region, size, global best-practice, and custom peer groups) • Recognition message analysis (quality, specificity, linkage to values) • Stakeholder interviews with HR, business leaders, and program administrators • Voice-of-employee insights (fairness, visibility, emotional connect), supplemented by the GPTW–VC R&R Scorecard where applicable • Platform and process diagnostics highlighting friction points and underutilised features • Recommendations from our R&R Advisor (beta), which synthesises global AIRᵉ patterns to highlight structural and behavioural improvements This multi-layered assessment surfaces both immediate improvement opportunities and systemic design gaps. We then design a transformation roadmap covering program design changes, feature enhancements, governance improvements, communication plans, manager enablement, and AIRᵉ-aligned recommendations that reflect what the most effective global recognition cultures do differently. |  | Benchmarking: Saurabh |  |  |  | I added Mercer's benchmarking at the top of this answer and modified the first sentence of Saurabh's answer so that it would flow. |  |  |

Recommendations are prioritized based on impact analysis and our assessment of Wells Fargo's readiness, ensuring alignment with organizational capacity and strategic objectives. Vantage Circle and Mercer will present these findings during a 3 hour current state review and recommendationas presentation. Vantage Circle will incoroprate Mercer's findings and recommendations into design sessions to create the future state of Wells Fargo's recognition program with consideration of their cutting edge technology. We use the AIRe Framework as the foundation, ensuring enhancements strengthen Appreciation, Incentivization, Reinforcement, and eMotional Connect while improving Authenticity and Impact. Actionable Recommendations: Based on the assessment, we create a prioritized improvement plan that addresses design gaps (award architecture, criteria, governance), behavioral reinforcement (values, consistency, fairness), and emotional connection (visibility, personalisation, specificity of messages). We also incorporate insights from high-effectiveness global AIRe benchmarks and the R&R Advisor (beta) recommendations. Frameworks and Best Practices: Our roadmap is guided by four layers: - AIRe for program design structure and behavioural-science alignment - WISE for technology and product recommendations (Workflow, Integrations, Social, Emotional layers) - REACH to ensure recommendations are grounded in research, advisory experience, and global insights - EDGE for best-in class program awareness, affinity and adoption support - Best practices from high-performing programs identified through our AIRe global dataset, annual reports, and peer comparisons The final roadmap includes quick wins, medium-term enhancements, and longer-term strategic changes, along with owner assignments and recommended metrics to track progress. This ensures Wells Fargo has a clear, evidence-backed path to achieving best-in-class recognition performance. |  | Benchmarking: Saurabh |  |  |  | I added Mercer's benchmarking at the top of this answer and modified the first sentence of Saurabh's answer so that it would flow. |  |  |
| 3.7 | Please describe your approach to evaluating and transforming an existing recognition program to achieve best-in-class status. In your response, address the following:  Integration of Existing Elements: How will you determine which current program elements should be retained, modified, or retired?  How will you ensure continuity for elements that are valued by our employees and stakeholders? | Vantage Circle will partner with Mercer as a subcontractor to provide program recommendations. Mercer evaluates program elements through a combination of employee feedback, usage data, and alignment with strategic objectives to determine their value and effectiveness. Elements that drive engagement and resonate with organizational culture are retained, while underperforming or outdated components are identified for modification or retirement. Mercer employs a decision matrix assessing value, cost, and impact to guide these decisions. To ensure continuity, Mercer engages stakeholders throughout the process and implements phased transitions supported by clear communication, training, and change management, thereby maintaining program momentum and employee trust.  Additionally, we will build upon Mercer's recommendations with more evaluation of existing program elements through an AIRe-based lens, combining design assessment, platform diagnostics, and employee/stakeholder insights to determine which elements should be retained, modified, or retired. Retain / Modify / Retire Decisions: Each current component - eCards, manager awards, milestones, retirement, events, communications, workflows is evaluated against: •	AIRe design quality: Does it strengthen Appreciation, Incentivization, Reinforcement, or eMotional Connect? •	Effectiveness metrics: Adoption, giver/receiver coverage, mix, message quality, equity, redemption patterns, budget efficiency. •	Employee experience: Feedback from the GPTW–VC R&R Scorecard, VOE insights, sentiment on fairness and emotional connect. •	Benchmark comparisons: How the element performs relative to high-effectiveness programs and similar global enterprises. •	Friction analysis: Operational complexity, approval bottlenecks, low-usage segments, or redundant processes. Elements that score well on behavioural impact and employee value are retained and strengthened; those with potential are redesigned or repositioned; and those consistently under-performing or duplicative are phased out or replaced. Ensuring Continuity: We protect continuity by identifying “high-equity” elements—those that employees and leaders value—and ensuring these are preserved, rebranded thoughtfully, or enhanced without disrupting familiarity. Communication plans, leader cascades, and transition guides ensure smooth change management. Where modifications are needed, we maintain the core experience while improving usability, criteria clarity, visibility, and emotional resonance. This approach ensures that the program evolves without losing the elements that make it meaningful to Wells Fargo employees and stakeholders. |  | Benchmarking: Saurabh |  |  |  | I added Mercer's benchmarking at the top of this answer and modified the first sentence of Saurabh's answer so that it would flow. |  |  |

Where program changes are significant, we recommend a phased implementation to preserve continuity, minimize disruption, and build confidence across employee groups. | 3.11 | How does your platform support business-specific recognition campaigns, custom award naming, and group-level branding within a single, unified recognition program? What strategies, features, or best practices do you recommend to ensure employees and administrators can easily navigate, understand, and participate in these customized efforts - without confusion or loss of program identity? Please address the following:  How your solution manages multiple award names, legacy awards, and business-specific campaigns within a single platform. | Our platform supports business-specific recognition campaigns, custom award naming, and group-level branding within a unified enterprise program through a Core + Custom architecture. This ensures each business unit can express its unique identity while maintaining a consistent, values-aligned global framework. 1. Managing Multiple Award Names & Legacy Awards All awards whether enterprise, BU-specific, or legacy are configured within a single structured awards library, governed by: •	Global naming conventions •	Standardized award descriptions •	Clear behavioural criteria •	Value-linked #tags to maintain alignment This prevents fragmentation and ensures that even legacy awards reinforce core values and behavioural expectations. 2. BU-Level Campaigns & Thematic Programs Campaign Management enables business units to run custom recognition drives (e.g., customer success campaigns, innovation sprints, culture weeks) with: •	Custom badges •	Group-level branding •	Targeted audiences •	BU-specific messaging These campaigns coexist within the global program but are nested under the parent framework, ensuring easy navigation and zero confusion. 3. Strategies to Prevent Confusion & Maintain Program Identity We maintain clarity through: •	A unified global framework (values, #tags, naming logic) •	Role- and BU-based visibility that employees only see the awards and campaigns relevant to them •	Clear categorization of enterprise awards vs. BU-specific awards •	Consistent UX patterns across all awards •	Leaderboards, social feeds, and Boost actions that reinforce enterprise culture regardless of BU customisation 4. Using #Tags to Standardize Meaning Across Teams Even when awards are BU-specific, #tags ensure every recognition moment is mapped back to the same set of enterprise values and behaviours. This prevents BU autonomy from diluting global culture and enables cross-team comparability. 5. Behaviour Reinforcement with Profile Badges Across multiple BUs, Profile Badges create a global behavioural currency. Employees who consistently demonstrate behaviours earn the same badges across all groups, preserving fairness and motivating consistent participation. 6. Intelligent Tools to Reduce Administrator & Manager Complexity •	Dynamic award search & filtering •	Admin guardrails to avoid duplicates / naming confusion •	AI-based Recognition Guide to improve message specificity •	Boost for leadership-level reinforcement without creating new award types These ensure that even with hundreds of awards or campaigns, the experience remains simple and intuitive. 7. Best Practices for Complex, Multi-BU Organizations We recommend: •	Enterprise-wide value system with a flexible BU layer •	Standard naming templates to avoid award clutter •	Controlled BU-level autonomy with global governance •	Periodic rationalization of legacy awards through our Program Audit •	Targeted campaigns for business lines with unique cultural or operational contexts (e.g., operations, captive centers, technology, risk) |  | Benchmarking: Saurabh |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 3.12 | How does your platform support business-specific recognition campaigns, custom award naming, and group-level branding within a single, unified recognition program? What strategies, features, or best practices do you recommend to ensure employees and administrators can easily navigate, understand, and participate in these customized efforts - without confusion or loss of program identity? Please address the following:  How you prevent confusion for employees, managers, and vendors when searching for or redeeming awards. | Our platform supports business-specific award names, campaigns, and group-level branding within a unified enterprise program through a structured Core + Custom architecture, while ensuring employees can easily understand award origins, eligibility, and redemption rules. We prevent confusion through a combination of award categorization, role-based visibility, intelligent search, and consistent behavioural tagging: 1. Clear Award Categorization & Origin Labels All awards whether enterprise, BU-specific, legacy, or campaign-based are organized within a single structured awards library with origin labels, award owners (BU/function), distinct icons, and clear descriptions. Employees always know where an award comes from and who it is meant for. 2. Smart Search & Advanced Filters Employees and managers can search and filter awards by name, BU, location, job level, and award type. They can also view “awards I can give” or “awards I’m eligible to receive,” ensuring they only interact with relevant awards and campaigns. 3. Role-Based Visibility & Eligibility Controls Awards and campaigns are only visible to eligible employees based on BU, geography, role, job level, or other configured rules. This avoids clutter, mis-selection, and incorrect nominations or redemptions. 4. Values-Linked #Tags to Standardize Meaning Even when BUs use different award names, #tags ensure every recognition maps back to the same enterprise values or behaviours. This maintains a unified cultural message and prevents employees from misinterpreting the purpose of an award. 5. Group-Level Branding With Consistent UI BUs can apply custom icons or campaign visuals, but all awards follow consistent UX patterns and platform layouts. This balances local identity with global cohesion so employees never feel like they are navigating disconnected programs. 6. Clear and Simple Redemption Experience All award points flow into a single balance. Employees see only the reward catalogue relevant to their geography, and the source award remains visible, preventing confusion about value, purpose, or eligibility during redemption. 7. Administrative Guardrails to Avoid Award Clutter We provide naming standards, required descriptions/#tags, campaign timing controls, and the ability to archive or sunset outdated awards. This ensures a clean, easy-to-navigate awards ecosystem. Together, these features ensure employees, managers, and administrators always know what an award is, who owns it, whether they are eligible, and how to participate, while preserving the integrity of one unified recognition program across multiple business units. |  | Benchmarking: Saurabh |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Award Categorization & Clear Origin Labelling All awards whether enterprise-wide, BU-specific, legacy, or campaign-based are organized within a single, structured awards library with: • Parent category (Enterprise \| Business Unit \| Campaign) • Award owner (e.g., Risk, Technology, Shared Services, Retail Ops) • Eligibility rules (role, BU, geography, level) • Value-linked #tags This ensures employees always know who the award belongs to and who it applies to.  2. Eligibility Controls & Role-Based Visibility Awards and campaigns are shown only for eligible employees based on configured rules (department, BU, country, job code, cost center). This ensures: • Nominators can never nominate for awards the nominee is not eligible for • BUs can run targeted campaigns without affecting the global experience • Program identity stays intact even with high customization  4. #Tag Framework for Consistent Meaning Across Groups Even when awards differ by BU, #tags link every recognition to the same enterprise values or behaviours. Communication Templates & Dynamic Guidance Admins can use: • Customizable campaign templates • Pre-defined award descriptions • Announcement modules with tailored audiences These make campaign launches clean, predictable, and easy for employees to understand.  6. Profile Badges as a Global Behaviour Currency Regardless of BU-level customization, Profile Badges are earned the same way across the company. This gives employees a shared recognition language that unifies the program even when awards differ.  7. Admin Guardrails to Prevent Fragmentation We provide admin tools to: • Prevent duplicate or confusing award names • Apply naming templates • Enforce consistent criteria and descriptions • Automatically archive or sunset legacy awards This keeps the ecosystem clean and easy to navigate.  In Summary We support business-specific awards and campaigns while maintaining global consistency through a combination of award categorization, #tag alignment, role-based visibility, structured eligibility rules, intelligent search/filters, communication templates, and admin governance. This ensures employees always know where an award originated, who it applies to, and how to participate without losing the integrity of the unified recognition program. |  | Benchmarking: Saurabh |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 4.1 | Please describe your platform’s policy and process for handling recognition points when an employee leaves Wells Fargo (due to termination, retirement, or other separation). Specifically:  What options are available for the employee to redeem any remaining points after their departure? | Vantage Circle does not retain any breakage on unredeemed points. Under our standard program design, points do not expire for active employees unless a client chooses to introduce a custom expiry period based on their internal requirements. Upon employee separation, we follow a clear and consistent process - aligned to the client’s program rules - to manage point validity and redemption timelines. This ensures full transparency and gives employees a fair opportunity to redeem their earned rewards.  Our Post-Separation Handling Framework includes two primary redemption pathways, depending on the nature of separation.  A. Voluntary Separations: For employees who resign voluntarily: Proactive Reminders: - Automated reminders prompt the departing employee to redeem their remaining points before their final working day.  Default Digital Gift Card Conversion: - If any points remain unredeemed at the time of separation, we issue a default Visa/Mastercard digital gift card loaded with the points balance.  Service Fee: - A flat 6.5% service fee is applied (on Gift card balance) to cover fulfillment and supporting documentation. The fee can be client-paid or deducted from the card value.  Delivery Options: The card can be delivered directly to the departing employee or shared with the Wells Fargo program owner based on preference.  B. Involuntary (Employer-Triggered) Separations  For employer-initiated separations - Any unredeemed balance is automatically converted to a default Visa/Mastercard digital gift card.  The gift card (balance with the adjustement of 6.5% fee) is issued to Wells Fargo, allowing the organization to deliver it to the former employee in accordance with internal policy.  This process ensures fair treatment, regulatory alignment, and a consistent experience for all employees while upholding Wells Fargo’s governance and audit needs.  C. For termed employees who are eligible for a service/retirement award, we leave the option to the employer to decide how they would like us to treat such cases. As taxation hasn't occured, it is not mandatory to deliver the service award. For programs like service/retirement awards that are billed on redemption there is naturally no scope to retain breakage. |  | Vijay/Prashansa |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 4.2 | Please describe your platform’s policy and process for handling recognition points when an employee leaves Wells Fargo (due to termination, retirement, or other separation). Specifically:  Is there a grace period or specific process for redemption post-termination? | Yes. Vantage Circle follows a clear, structured process to ensure departing employees are treated fairly and consistently. In line with our policy outlined above, the post-termination process differs for voluntary and involuntary separations.  1) Voluntary Separations  Grace Period Prior to Final Day: Departing employees receive automated reminders before their last working day encouraging them to redeem any remaining points.  Optional Limited Access: Wells Fargo may choose to provide limited redemption access up to the employee’s final day of employment.  No Post-Termination Grace Window: Once employment ends, platform access is removed and any remaining balance is converted to a default Visa/Mastercard digital gift card as described in Section 4.1.  2) Involuntary (Employer-Triggered) Separations: There is no grace period for redemption.  Unredeemed points are immediately converted to a default Visa/Mastercard digital gift card and delivered to Wells Fargo for onward distribution as described in Section 4.1.  - Consistent with Program Policy - Points never expire while the employee is active.  After separation, points are always resolved through redemption or default gift card issuance.  No breakage is retained under any circumstance.  This approach provides a consistent, compliant, and fully auditable process while giving Wells Fargo flexibility in how they wish to handle voluntary separation scenarios. |  | Vijay/Prashansa |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 4.3 | Please describe your platform’s policy and process for handling recognition points when an employee leaves Wells Fargo (due to termination, retirement, or other separation). Support Mechanism we provide:  - Simple step-by-step instructions - Direct links to the rewards catalog - Automated reminders until the final working day - Final notifications confirming conversion to a default digital gift card (if points remain unredeemed)  Default Gift Card Support: If points convert automatically:  Employees (or Wells Fargo, depending on the scenario) receive the Visa/Mastercard digital card along with supporting documentation and activation instructions.  Our support team is available to assist with any redemption questions or card-related queries. | 4.9 | Please describe your platform’s process and best practices for testing and releasing system updates:  What is your standard update cycle, including the steps from development to testing to production? | Vantage Circle has a rigorous and structured process for testing and releasing system updates, ensuring high-quality and stable software delivery. Our standard quarterly update cycle includes several key steps:  • Code Reviews: Every change undergoes thorough peer review to maintain code quality, security, and consistency before any further testing. • Developer Testing: Developers conduct unit and integration tests to validate functional correctness locally before submitting code. • Quality Assurance (QA): Dedicated QA teams execute comprehensive test plans covering functionality, performance, and security in controlled environments to identify any issues. • User Acceptance Testing (UAT): Selected users, often clients or power users, validate the system against real-world scenarios to ensure business requirements are met. • Production Release: Only after passing all prior stages, releases are deployed to the production environment in a controlled manner, with monitoring for any post-release issues.  This multi-layered process minimizes risk and ensures that updates deliver value reliably while maintaining platform stability and user satisfaction. |  | Solution & Technical Queries: Hemanga |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 4.20 | Describe how your platform manages nomination permissions and approval routing using employee hierarchy data (e.g., from Workday). In your response, address:  How nomination rights can be configured so only designated roles (e.g., specific manager levels) can issue monetary or points-based awards. | When integrating with a Human Capital Management system (HCM) such as Workday, the system performs a secure data synchronization process to retrieve and maintain up-to-date employee information. The data captured during this integration is strictly limited to the attributes necessary for the functioning of the recognition or rewards platform.  The typical employee attributes retrieved include: ⦁ Employee identifiers such as Employee Name and Employee ID ⦁ Organizational hierarchy details including Reporting Manager’s Name and Email Address ⦁ Job-related metadata such as Level, Grade, or Group Classification ⦁ It is important to note that no confidential or personally sensitive information—such as compensation data, personal contact information, government identifiers, or demographic details—is captured or stored during this integration. All data exchange adheres to standard data privacy, encryption, and access control protocols to ensure compliance with organizational and regulatory requirements.  Following the HCM integration, program configuration activities are carried out in collaboration with program administrators or business stakeholders. The platform enables flexible award visibility and access management, allowing administrators to determine which employee segments can view or submit nominations for specific awards.  Awards can be configured to: ⦁ Be visible or open for nomination to all employees across the organization, or ⦁ Be restricted to specific roles, functions, or hierarchical levels, such as junior, mid-level, or senior management groups. ⦁ Furthermore, eligibility and access filters can be independently defined at both the nominator and recipient levels. Such a control ensures precision in governance. For instance, restricting certain awards so that only designated leadership roles can nominate, while eligibility for receiving those awards may be limited to particular business units or employee hierarchical levels.  This configurability allows organizations to maintain consistency with internal recognition policies while ensuring that the award workflows remain equitable, secure, and operationally aligned with business objectives. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 4.21 | Describe how your platform manages nomination permissions and approval routing using employee hierarchy data (e.g., from Workday). In your response, address:  How your platform accommodates varying approval flows across business units or organizational levels, including exceptions and custom configurations. | When integrating with a Human Capital Management system (HCM) such as Workday, the system performs a secure data synchronization process to retrieve and maintain up-to-date employee information. The data captured during this integration is strictly limited to the attributes necessary for the functioning of the recognition or rewards platform.  The typical employee attributes retrieved include: ⦁ Employee identifiers such as Employee Name and Employee ID ⦁ Organizational hierarchy details including Reporting Manager’s Name and Email Address ⦁ Job-related metadata such as Level, Grade, or Group Classification ⦁ It is important to note that no confidential or personally sensitive information—such as compensation data, personal contact information, government identifiers, or demographic details—is captured or stored during this integration. All data exchange adheres to standard data privacy, encryption, and access control protocols to ensure compliance with organizational and regulatory requirements.  The platform supports multiple award approval workflows that can be configured based on the award type, monetary value, and organizational governance policies. The following approval options are typically available:  1. Auto-Approval: This workflow is generally applied to low-value awards (typically in the range of $10–$25) or for non-recurring recognition activities that do not require managerial validation. Common use cases include: ⦁ Awards for new hires or rehires ⦁ One-time initiatives such as holiday gifting or hackathon participation ⦁ Department- or team-specific celebrations and engagement activities  2. Single-Level (First-Level) Approval: This workflow is used for moderate-value awards, typically ranging between $25 and $500, where managerial review is required before issuance. The approving authority is generally the employee’s immediate reporting manager or business unit head.  3. Multi-Level Approval (Two or More Levels): High-value or prestigious awards, generally exceeding $500, may require two or more levels of sequential approval. The approval hierarchy can be configured based on organizational structure, for example, manager → department head → HR or program administrator, thereby ensuring appropriate oversight and budget control.  4. Panel-Based Awards: For awards that rely on peer evaluation or committee-based decision-making, a panel workflow can be configured. In this setup: ⦁ Nominations are submitted through the platform and routed to a predefined panel of evaluators or voters. ⦁ Each panel may be unique to a department, business unit, or line of business, allowing for contextualized evaluation. ⦁ After voting and deliberation, a designated winner selector or approver finalizes the selection and formally approves the award.  This flexible workflow configuration ensures that the award governance structure aligns with both organizational recognition strategy and compliance requirements, while maintaining efficiency across varying award types and values. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 4.22 | Describe how your platform manages nomination permissions and approval routing using employee hierarchy data (e.g., from Workday). In your response, address:  How hierarchy data is imported, synchronized, and dynamically updated to reflect organizational changes (e.g., transfers, promotions). | The integration with Workday has been developed in line with Workday’s best practices, leveraging the Report as a Service (RaaS) approach. A custom Workday report is created to include all the required data fields, which is then exposed as an API for the platform to consume. Authentication for this API can be configured using either basic authentication (username and password) or OAuth for enhanced security. Appropriate report-level security permissions ensure that only the defined fields are accessible through the API. Platform can invoke the Report API on demand to retrieve data from Workday. The extracted data represents a complete dataset of all eligible employees, as the integration performs a full data sync rather than a delta (incremental) sync.  This automated synchronization eliminates the need for manual intervention and ensures that the employee’s profile within the platform remains accurate and aligned with the organization’s source-of-truth system.  Example Scenarios Change in Manager or Team Structure: When an existing employee transitions to a new team or reports to a different manager, the update recorded in Workday is automatically fetched through the API. The platform reflects these changes seamlessly, updating the employee’s reporting line, hierarchy, and related access permissions. Consequently, any new award nominations or submissions initiated by this employee will automatically follow the updated reporting structure and approval workflow.  Promotion or Role Elevation: In cases where an employee is promoted from a non-managerial to a managerial role, the updated grade or level information is also synchronized. Post-sync, the employee gains enhanced visibility and access rights corresponding to their new role such as the ability to view or approve awards that were previously restricted to higher management.  Employee Lifecycle Events: For new joiners, profiles are created automatically upon addition to the HCM, while for employees exiting the organization, their access is revoked or deactivated based on the termination data synced from the HCM.  This real-time data consistency ensures operational accuracy across recognition workflows, minimizes administrative overhead, and upholds the integrity of program governance by ensuring that all award submissions, approvals, and eligibility filters operate on the most current organizational data. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 4.23 | Describe how your platform manages nomination permissions and approval routing using employee hierarchy data (e.g., from Workday). In your response, address:  What controls exist to enforce role-based restrictions and manage changes to permissions over time. | The platform supports a role-based access control model, ensuring that each user’s permissions and visibility are aligned with their responsibilities and level of engagement within the rewards and recognition program. Different roles can be assigned based on organizational hierarchy, function, and operational requirement.  The key roles include:  1. Super Admin This role is designated for program administrators and primary stakeholders responsible for the overall governance and management of the recognition platform. Super Admins have full system access, including the ability to: ⦁ Configure and manage awards, approval workflows, and eligibility criteria ⦁ Oversee and report on organization-wide R&R activities ⦁ Manage user roles and permissions, budget management ⦁ Access analytics and dashboards for tracking program performance  2. HR Admin The HR Admin role is typically assigned to department heads, HR Business Partners (HRBPs), or HR program coordinators. This role allows access to department- or region-specific data and activities, enabling them to: ⦁ Review and monitor recognition trends within their function or business unit ⦁ Oversee department-specific awards and nominations ⦁ Generate reports and insights for their respective teams ⦁ Support budget, compliance and governance at the functional level  3. Nominator The Nominator role is granted to users who meet the predefined nomination filter criteria (e.g., tenure, role level, or business function). These users can: ⦁ Submit nominations for eligible awards ⦁ Provide supporting details, justifications, or attachments during nomination ⦁ View the nomination history of awards where they have participated  4. Approver The Approver role is assigned to individuals who have the authority to review and approve award nominations. Approvers are typically line managers or designated leaders and can: ⦁ Review nominations routed to them through the approval workflow ⦁ Approve or reject awards based on eligibility and program guidelines ⦁ Add comments or feedback as part of the approval process  This tiered role structure provides granular control, data security, and operational transparency, ensuring that every user has access strictly aligned with their role in the recognition lifecycle from program management to nomination, review, and final approval. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 4.25 | Describe how your platform manages nomination permissions and approval routing using employee hierarchy data (e.g., from Workday). In your response, address:  How your platform ensures privacy and security of hierarchy data during routing and approval processes. | Our platform is designed with a strong focus on data privacy, confidentiality, and security, particularly concerning organizational hierarchy and employee information used in nomination routing and award approvals. The following mechanisms and practices ensure the protection of hierarchy data throughout the recognition workflow:  1. Role-Based Access Control All user access to hierarchy and organizational data is strictly governed by role-based permissions. Only authorized roles such as Super Admins, HR Admins, or designated Approvers can view or act upon hierarchy information relevant to their responsibilities. Users with nominator or recipient roles only access the data required for their participation (e.g., their own team or eligible award pool), preventing exposure to unrelated organizational structures.  2. Data Minimization and Scope Limitation The platform only captures essential hierarchy information needed for routing and approvals, such as reporting lines, employee ID, role, and department. Sensitive personal information or confidential data (e.g., compensation, personal identifiers, or performance scores) is never included in routing or workflow data. This ensures that workflow processes operate on minimal necessary data, reducing exposure risk.  3. Secure Routing and Approval Workflows Award nominations and approvals are routed automatically and internally based on the verified organizational hierarchy retrieved from the HCM (e.g., Workday). Routing logic ensures that employees can only see or approve awards for which they are eligible, eliminating inadvertent data exposure. All workflow actions like submissions, approvals, or rejections are logged in audit trails for accountability.  4. Data Encryption and Secure Storage Hierarchy and workflow data are stored using industry-standard encryption both at rest and in transit. Access to the data is controlled via secure authentication mechanisms such as SSO Logs and audit trails are maintained in a tamper-proof manner, ensuring that all access and changes to hierarchy data can be traced and reviewed.  5. Compliance and Governance The platform adheres to established data privacy and regulatory frameworks, including GDPR, SOC 2, and ISO 27001 standards. Regular audits and access reviews are conducted to ensure that hierarchy data exposure is limited strictly to the purpose of nomination routing, approval processing, and program governance. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 4.49 | Does your platform allow the recipient of an eCard to reply directly to the sender within the platform? In your response, please describe:  Whether the reply is sent automatically through the platform or requires manual steps. | Vantage Circle’s platform supports multiple types of recognition posts including Award posts, Badge posts, and Greetings, each providing distinct interaction capabilities:  Award Post & Badge Post: These recognitions are posted directly on the social feed unless given privately. When visible on the feed, recipients can visit the platform and reply to the sender through comments seamlessly within the platform. This creates an interactive and engaging experience.  Greetings: Greetings are delivered privately via email and do not appear on the social feed. Since they are private, replies to greetings are not supported within the platform.  In summary, replies to Award and Badge posts are sent automatically through the platform and can be made via comments, while Greetings are private and email-delivered without reply functionality within the platform. |  | Solution & Technical Queries: Hemanga |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

For Award posts and Badge posts that are shared on the social recognition feed, recipients can comment directly on the post. When a recipient replies:  • The sender is notified both within the platform through an in-app notification and via email. • The reply appears as a comment on the original recognition post on the feed, making it easy for the sender to find and respond if needed.  However, for private Greetings, which are delivered directly via email and not posted on the feed, replies within the platform are not supported.  This setup facilitates meaningful, timely two-way interactions around recognition that are visible and trackable for the entire team while respecting privacy when needed. |  | Solution & Technical Queries: Hemanga |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 4.54 | Is badging functionality presented directly within your platform, integrated with Workday, or both? | The Integration built with Workday will be bidirectional. The outbound integration from Workday will be built as a RaaS (Report as a Service) that will be exposed as an API to Vantage so that relevant Employee Data can be passed . Any new hires and existing employees will be sent across using this integration to Vantage Circle.  Similarly Workday web services will be utilized to push the badge and award data of employees from Vantage Circle so that their employee performance profiles in Workday are updated.   Currently, profile badges are awarded and displayed exclusively within the platform. A badge is granted to a user when they rank in the top 10% for a selected behavior or attribute within their organization over the preceding quarter. This provides a visual recognition of high performers and reinforces positive behaviors aligned with organizational values.  We have submitted a request to enable badge visibility within Microsoft Teams calls, allowing users to showcase their achievements directly in collaboration sessions. This request is presently under review with the Microsoft App Certification team, and we are awaiting approval before this functionality can be rolled out externally.  We are actively working to extend the profile badging functionality into the Performance Management within Workday. This enhancement will allow badges and award-related activities earned on our platform to be reflected directly within an employee’s Workday profile, providing a holistic view of recognition and performance achievements. Achieving this requires a two-way integration between our platform and the organization’s Workday instance:  ⦁ Outbound: Workday will provide updated employee records, ensuring that award and badge visibility remains aligned with changes in hierarchy, role, or organizational structure. ⦁ Inbound: Badge and award data from our platform will be transmitted to Workday to update employee performance profiles.  This integration will create a seamless experience, allowing recognition activity to be tracked, measured, and incorporated into formal performance assessments, thereby strengthening the link between employee engagement, recognition, and performance management. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 4.62 | How does your platform integrate with Workday to enable sending an eCard to all direct reports or all employees reporting to a specific manager? Please describe: The integration process with Workday, including how employee hierarchy data (manager, direct reports, reporting structure) is imported, synchronized, and maintained. | The integration developed with Workday follows Workday’s best practices and leverages the Report as a Service (RaaS) approach. A custom report is created within Workday containing all the required data fields, which is then exposed as an API for the Vantage system to consume.  Authentication for this API can be configured using either basic authentication (username and password) or OAuth for enhanced security. The report is secured with appropriate access permissions, ensuring that only the defined fields are available for extraction through the API. The Vantage system can invoke the Report API on demand to retrieve data from Workday. The integration performs a full data sync of all eligible employee records, not a delta (incremental) sync.  The integration between Workday and platform is designed to be bidirectional. The outbound integration from Workday—built using RaaS—enables Workday to expose relevant employee data to platform, covering both new hires and existing employees. In turn, Workday web services are utilized for the inbound integration, allowing platform to send badge and award data back to Workday, ensuring that employee performance profiles within Workday remain up to date.  The platform can be used to appreciate, nominate or send a private greeting. Single user or multiple users can receive the badges, awards together.  Employees can send private greetings directly to any colleague within the organization. Organizations have the flexibility to enable or disable this feature based on their engagement strategy. Greetings available in the platform’s catalog can be customized to reflect organizational themes such as Thank You, Congratulations, or Diversity and Inclusion initiatives, allowing for tailored messaging aligned with company values.  Service Milestone Recognition via Service Yearbook For employees achieving service milestones, the platform automatically generates a Service Yearbook delivered on their anniversary date. The Service Yearbook compiles personalized messages from leadership, peers, colleagues, and managers, creating a meaningful and memorable recognition experience. Program stakeholders have the flexibility to define the scope of participation for each milestone celebration, choosing whether messages are collected from: ⦁ Immediate reportees ⦁ All employees within the organization ⦁ Specific teams or departments  This combination of private eGreetings and milestone celebrations enhances employee engagement, strengthens organizational culture, and provides a structured yet personalized approach to recognizing contributions across the organization. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal | ` |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 4.65 | How does your platform integrate with Workday to enable sending an eCard to all direct reports or all employees reporting to a specific manager? Please describe: How the platform ensures data accuracy and timely updates when organizational changes occur in Workday. | The integration with Workday has been developed in line with Workday’s best practices, leveraging the Report as a Service (RaaS) approach. A custom Workday report is created to include all the required data fields, which is then exposed as an API for the platform to consume. Authentication for this API can be configured using either basic authentication (username and password) or OAuth for enhanced security. Appropriate report-level security permissions ensure that only the defined fields are accessible through the API. Platform can invoke the Report API on demand to retrieve data from Workday. The extracted data represents a complete dataset of all eligible employees, as the integration performs a full data sync rather than a delta (incremental) sync.  This automated synchronization eliminates the need for manual intervention and ensures that the employee’s profile within the platform remains accurate and aligned with the organization’s source-of-truth system.  Example Scenarios Change in Manager or Team Structure: When an existing employee transitions to a new team or reports to a different manager, the update recorded in Workday is automatically fetched through the API. The platform reflects these changes seamlessly, updating the employee’s reporting line, hierarchy, and related access permissions. Consequently, any new award nominations or submissions initiated by this employee will automatically follow the updated reporting structure and approval workflow.  Promotion or Role Elevation: In cases where an employee is promoted from a non-managerial to a managerial role, the updated grade or level information is also synchronized. Post-sync, the employee gains enhanced visibility and access rights corresponding to their new role such as the ability to view or approve awards that were previously restricted to higher management.  Employee Lifecycle Events: For new joiners, profiles are created automatically upon addition to the HCM, while for employees exiting the organization, their access is revoked or deactivated based on the termination data synced from the HCM.  This real-time data consistency ensures operational accuracy across recognition workflows, minimizes administrative overhead, and upholds the integrity of program governance by ensuring that all award submissions, approvals, and eligibility filters operate on the most current organizational data. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal |  | Feel like we aren't answering the question directly with sufficient details |  |  |  |  |  |

| 4.102 | Historically, our organization delivered physical recognition banners and pins to employees for multiple achievements, years of service, and contributions. | 4.108 | We have seen interest in challenge coins as a recognition tool. What experience does your organization have with challenge coins for employee recognition? Interest often emerges organically from veterans, reservists, or teams that value tradition and camaraderie. These items can be integrated seamlessly into the digital platform experience, allowing leaders to: • Tell the story behind the coin • Recognize the specific behavior or accomplishment • Create a meaningful moment of presentation If challenge coins are culturally aligned with Wells Fargo’s employee values and traditions, we can partner with your teams to design a coin-based recognition element that fits naturally into your broader Recognition & Rewards strategy. | 4.113 | Please describe your platform’s incident response process in the event of a data breach or system outage. Please describe the configuration process, supported protocols (e.g., SAML, OAuth), and any limitations. | Yes, Vantage Circle supports Single Sign-On (SSO) via Azure Active Directory (now Microsoft Entra ID), using standard SAML 2.0 and OAuth 2.0 protocols. The configuration involves exchanging metadata or configuration details such as Entity ID, ACS URL, and certificate, which are set up in both the client’s Entra ID and the Vantage Circle admin console. Once configured, users can log in seamlessly using their corporate credentials, enabling secure and centralized access management. SSO enforcement is also supported for restricting access exclusively through the organization's identity provider. | 4.134 | Please describe your platform’s authentication capabilities for employee access. In your response, address: Examples: Please provide case studies or screenshots illustrating SSO and external login workflows. | Our platform provides Single Sign-On (SSO) through SAML 2.0 and OAuth 2.0, enabling users to log in using their organization’s existing identity provider such as Azure Active Directory, Okta, Google Workspace, or Microsoft Entra ID. External logins are fully supported, allowing employees to use federated credentials without the need to create separate platform passwords.  All authentication requests are encrypted in transit via HTTPS/TLS 1.2+, and session tokens are securely managed using short-lived access tokens with refresh capabilities. Multi-Factor Authentication (MFA) can be enforced through the client’s IdP configuration.  Vantage Circle also supports role-based access control (RBAC), ensuring users have access only to features and data relevant to their assigned role.  There are three screenshots attached as evidence. The first one shows the initial 2-Factor Verification screen where the user is prompted to enter the 5-digit verification code that has been sent to their registered email address. This screen is presented immediately after the user attempts to log in and serves as the entry point for the OTP-based authentication flow. The second screenshot displays the OTP email received by the user. This email contains the one-time password along with the validity period and instructions for support in case of any issues. This demonstrates that the OTP is successfully generated and delivered to the user’s inbox as part of the secure login process. The third screenshot shows the outcome when an incorrect or expired OTP is entered on the verification screen. The interface displays clear error messages such as “Incorrect verification code” and “Token expired. Please try again,” indicating that the system correctly validates the OTP and prevents unauthorized access. | 4.140 | Please describe your platform’s capabilities for integrating with Workday. In your response, address: Predesigned Integrations: Do you offer any Workday-certified or prebuilt integrations for recognition, rewards, or employee data management? If so, please describe their features, technical specifications, and how they support real-time data exchange, program deployment, and compliance. | The integration developed with Workday follows Workday’s best practices and leverages the Report as a Service (RaaS) approach. A custom report is created within Workday containing all the required data fields, which is then exposed as an API for the Vantage system to consume.  Authentication for this API can be configured using either basic authentication (username and password) or OAuth for enhanced security. The report is secured with appropriate access permissions, ensuring that only the defined fields are available for extraction through the API. The Vantage system can invoke the Report API on demand to retrieve data from Workday. The integration performs a full data sync of all eligible employee records, not a delta (incremental) sync.  The integration between Workday and platform is designed to be bidirectional. The outbound integration from Workday—built using RaaS—enables Workday to expose relevant employee data to platform, covering both new hires and existing employees. In turn, Workday web services are utilized for the inbound integration, allowing platform to send badge and award data back to Workday, ensuring that employee performance profiles within Workday remain up to date.  Additional Steps :  The Workday applications team will need to build the report with the required fields for Vantage and appropriate filters.  Limitations of RaaS Integration: The data pulled from the Report API will always be most recent data as of the effective date and in case if any employee goes through multiple changes then only the latest change will be captured and updated into the system. Thus, any prior changes will not be trackable. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal |  | Looks like the same answer as above pasted here and this question has not been answered |  |  |  |  |  |
| 4.141 | Please describe your platform’s capabilities for integrating with Workday. In your response, address: Custom Integration Support: If predesigned integrations are not available, can your platform support custom-designed Workday integrations? Please outline your process for developing, testing, and maintaining custom integrations, including timelines, required resources, and ongoing support. | Our platform supports both standard and fully custom integrations with Workday. When a prebuilt connector is not available, we can design and implement a custom Workday integration that aligns with Workday’s best practices and your program requirements.  Following is our process to complete these integrations 1. Ability to Build Custom Workday Integrations Our platform can support custom-designed integrations using Workday’s available technologies, including: ⦁ Report as a Service (RaaS) APIs ⦁ Workday Web Services (SOAP/REST) ⦁ Custom data fields and calculated fields This allows us to accommodate any unique data structures, security models, or eligibility rules.  2. Custom Integration Development Process ⦁ Discovery & Requirements (1-2 weeks) Joint review of data needs (employee data, hierarchy, custom fields, status fields, etc.) Mapping required fields to Workday business objects Identifying outbound needs (Workday to VC Platform) and inbound requirements (VC Platform to Workday)  ⦁ Design & Configuration (2-4 weeks) Build custom Workday report(s) or web service configurations Set up authentication (OAuth, Basic Auth, or Workday-issued credentials) Create field mappings and data validation rules Configure error handling and retry logic  ⦁ Development & Internal Testing (2-3 weeks) Configure integration endpoints Validate sample data and transformations, award workflows to review all use cases are being addressed Review any workflow gaps or inconsistencies Conduct internal QA testing on both sides Ensure the solution meets Workday’s security and integration guidelines  ⦁ Preparation for integration in PROD (1-2 weeks) Once the results from previous stage are inline with expectations, look at promoting and replicating this integration in PROD environment  3. Required Resources Client-side: A Workday administrator or integration analyst to create/enhance reports, expose RaaS, and manage security groups/internal controls and some business users to overgo use case vs test data results. Platform-side: Integration specialists, QA analyst, implementation lead.  4. Ongoing Support & Maintenance Monitoring: Automated health checks and alerting for failed runs. Enhancements: Support for new fields, structural changes, or additional Workday business processes. Troubleshooting: Root-cause analysis for data mismatches or sync issues. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
