| 4.144 | Please describe your platform’s capabilities for integrating with Workday. In your response, address: Customer Experience: Please provide examples or case studies of successful Workday integrations with your platform, including implementation timelines, challenges addressed, and outcomes achieved. | To date, we have successfully executed Workday integrations for several customers, demonstrating our capability to handle diverse organizational contexts and integration scenarios. These projects have included: ⦁ Transitions from legacy HCM systems such as Oracle PeopleSoft to Workday. ⦁ Migration from SFTP-based integrations to a Workday-based integration model.  Our preferred integration approach leverages Workday’s Report-as-a-Service (RaaS) combined with OAuth-based authorization. This method provides a secure, read-only mechanism to access employee data required for program execution, ensuring that the information provided to the platform is limited in scope to the recognition program and adheres to organizational privacy and security policies.  Key Challenges and Considerations Each Workday integration presents unique challenges that require careful planning and execution: ⦁ Field Mapping: Ensuring accurate mapping of Workday fields to the platform’s data model to minimize overheads and maintain data integrity. ⦁ Hierarchical Data: Maintaining correct reporting lines and hierarchy levels that are used as filters for award access, ensuring seamless functionality before and after migration. ⦁ Employee Experience: Guaranteeing that employees’ experience on the platform remains consistent and uninterrupted, regardless of whether data is sourced from a legacy HCM or Workday. ⦁ Data Accuracy and Completeness: Validating that all relevant employee attributes (e.g., manager, level, department) are synchronized correctly and consistently across systems.  Through careful design, testing, and validation, these integrations ensure that organizational hierarchy, award eligibility, and user experience remain intact while transitioning to Workday, thereby minimizing disruption and maintaining program effectiveness. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 4.145 | Do you have the ability to distinguish populations based on Workday data including job code, status, termination date, level, employee type, and country for purposes of eligibility, access, and parity? | The integration developed within Workday leverages a Report-based Integration approach, utilizing Workday’s Report as a Service (RaaS) framework. At the core of this design is a custom report built on the Worker business object, ensuring that all relevant worker-level attributes are accurately captured.   This custom report can be further enhanced to include a wide range of filtering capabilities, such as job code, status, termination date, level, employee type, and country for purposes of eligibility, access, and parity. These filters provide flexibility to tailor the data extraction according to the consuming system’s specific needs.  Workday also offers multiple data source options within the Worker object such as Worker, All Active Employees, Contingent Workers, or other related datasets allowing the integration to be configured with the correct level of granularity and security. By using these curated data sources, the report can enforce appropriate access restrictions, ensuring that only allowed fields and records are exposed through the integration.  Overall, this approach provides a scalable, secure, and maintainable mechanism for generating Worker data for downstream systems while adhering to Workday best practices. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal |  | Can we directly reference all these fileds in our answer + 1 or 2 others: job code, status, termination date, level, employee type, and country for purposes of eligibility, access, and parity? |  |  |  |  |  |

| 4.147 | Please describe the tools and features your platform offers to align employee recognition with performance management and talent development frameworks. In your response, address: Integration Capabilities: How does your solution integrate with existing performance management systems (e.g., Workday) and talent development platforms? | The integrations designed with Workday will follow a bidirectional architecture, ensuring seamless data flow between Workday and Vantage.  On the outbound side, Workday will utilize a Report as a Service (RaaS)–based integration. A custom Workday report will be exposed as an API endpoint, enabling Vantage Circle to consume the required employee data in real time or on a scheduled basis. This outbound feed will capture both new hires and existing employees, ensuring that Vantage Circle always receives the most accurate and up-to-date employee information needed for processing recognition activities or other program requirements.  On the inbound side, Workday’s native web services (SOAP and/or REST) will be used to receive employee badge and award data transmitted from Vantage Circle. Once this data is received, it will be used to update the employee's performance profile, recognition history, or related worker-level attributes within Workday. This ensures that Workday reflects a complete and current view of each employee’s recognition achievements.  Both integration paths (outbound employee data and inbound recognition data) are designed in alignment with Workday best practices and recommended design patterns, ensuring scalability, security, and maintainability. By adhering to these standards, the solution minimizes custom complexity while maximizing reliability and long-term supportability.  Using these integrations, employee profiles on Workday can be updated with awards received, badges recognized, milestones completed. Through our profile badging solution, we can identify users who display a trait repeatedly over a course of time and update their Talet profile for those skills. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal |  | No mention of how the intregation can influence performance management systems and talent development platforms. | 4.152 | Please describe the tools and features your platform offers to align employee recognition with performance management and talent development frameworks. In your response, address: Best Practices & Examples: Please provide examples or case studies demonstrating how your solution has successfully supported the alignment of recognition with performance management and talent development in large organizations. | Alignment of Employee Recognition With Performance Management and Talent Development Vantage Circle’s Rewards & Recognition (R&R) platform provides a comprehensive, values-driven approach that directly supports organizational performance and talent development goals. The platform is designed to embed recognition into the daily flow of work while aligning it with core values, leadership competencies, and strategic performance expectations.  1. Values-Driven Award Framework Vantage Circle enables clients to define and operationalize their organizational values such as innovation, collaboration, customer focus, accountability, or leadership within the recognition ecosystem. Award structures and workflows are fully configurable, allowing each recognition moment to reinforce behaviors that matter most. Key Capabilities a) Custom Award Categories: Tailored award categories reflect each client’s cultural, behavioral, and performance priorities. This ensures recognition is not only celebratory but also tightly aligned with strategic objectives. b) Points-Based & Tiered Rewards:Employees earn points for demonstrating behaviors tied to organizational goals or competency models. Points can be redeemed for personalized rewards or used toward learning and development experiences directly supporting growth and career advancement. c) Real-Time Recognition:Managers and peers can acknowledge contributions instantly, reinforcing positive behaviors exactly when they occur and strengthening performance habits. d) Public Celebration Tools:Recognitions can be highlighted through social walls, announcements, and teams communication channels, amplifying cultural values and encouraging broader behavioral adoption. e) Recognition Campaigns:Organizations can create targeted recognition campaigns around quarterly goals, competency milestones, or talent initiatives. The platform provides built-in metrics to monitor participation, effectiveness, and business impact.  2. Goal & Competency Alignment Every recognition moment can be tagged to business goals, leadership behaviors, functional competencies, or project milestones. This structured alignment helps managers and HR teams link appreciation to performance expectations, enabling richer and more consistent development conversations throughout the year.  3. Integration With Performance & Talent Systems Vantage Circle integrates seamlessly with leading HCM, PMS, and LMS solutions including Workday, SuccessFactors, Oracle HCM, Darwinbox, and others to ensure recognition becomes an actionable component of the broader talent ecosystem. Examples of Use Cases Solved For a) Recognition linked to specific competencies can trigger relevant learning modules through the LMS. b) Recognition trends serve as inputs in talent reviews, succession planning, and calibration discussions. c) Data insights help HR and leaders identify emerging talent, high-performance patterns, and development gaps.  4. Manager Enablement for Continuous Feedback The platform supports managers with: a) Guided recognition templates b) Behavioral prompts c) Nudges to recognize under-represented or high-performing team members These encourage meaningful, equitable, and ongoing feedback, reducing bias and supporting continuous performance management.  5. Advanced Analytics & Dashboards Our analytics engine provides deep visibility into recognition behaviors across the organization. Key insights include aspects such as: a) Correlations between recognition frequency, performance outcomes b) Heatmaps showing values alignment across business units These insights support workforce planning, leadership development, and performance calibration cycles.  Upcoming Capabilities Strengthening Alignment With Performance & Talent Development As part of our Intelligent Recognition roadmap, we are introducing two capabilities that further deepen the connection between recognition, performance management, and talent development: SkillScape (Behaviour & Capability Mapping): SkillScape helps organisations understand where key values, behaviours, and emerging capabilities are concentrated across the workforce. By analysing #tag patterns, recognition frequency, and cross-team visibility, SkillScape surfaces “behaviour hotspots” that correlate with strong performance, highlights teams demonstrating core values consistently, and identifies individuals who may be emerging as high-potential talent. This becomes a valuable input into capability assessments, development planning, and succession pipelines.  Recognition Roll (Employee Narrative & Performance Storytelling): Recognition Roll creates a narrative for each employee — a full-year wrap of the recognition they’ve received. It brings pattern recognition into performance conversations: - What values do they demonstrate most consistently? - Which behaviours or strengths define them? - What accomplishments are they known for across teams or projects? This transforms recognition into performance storytelling, giving managers richer evidence for check-ins, development discussions, and talent reviews. Together, these roadmap features extend the platform’s role from recognition delivery to behavioural intelligence, strengthening Wells Fargo’s ability to link recognition to talent development, capability building, and long-term performance outcomes.  Best Practice Example: Global Technology Enterprise (230,000+ Employees)  Challenge The organization sought to strengthen and embed its cultural values expressed as the “Five Habits”: Being Respectful, Being Responsive, Always Communicating, Demonstrating Stewardship, and Building Trust across a large, globally distributed workforce. They required a recognition system capable of reinforcing these habits as daily behaviors rather than aspirational statements.  Approach a) Designed a values-based recognition framework fully mapped to the Five Habits. b) Implemented Unit Awards and SPOT Awards (monetary and non-monetary), each tied to demonstration of the Five Habit, in addition to Long Service Awards. c) Enabled real-time, peer-to-peer recognition to allow immediate appreciation across global teams. d) Integrated analytics and dashboards into performance review cycles, ensuring recognition data informed development discussions, goal alignment, and talent decisions.  Outcome / Impact a) Over 768 recognitions per day on average, with 553,490+ awards issued in two years, demonstrating enterprise-wide adoption. b) A 97.5% increase in non-monetary recognitions (badges and tokens) from 2022 to 2024, reflecting a cultural shift toward frequent, peer-led appreciation. c) In the most recent fiscal year, 57%+ of global employees received at least one recognition, averaging one recognition every 1.2 minutes. d) The program won Gold at the Brandon Hall HCM Excellence Awards for “Best Advance in Employee Recognition Program.” e) Embedding the Five Habits into recognition has translated the organization’s values into consistent daily behaviors, strengthening performance alignment and supporting long-term talent development. |  | Program Success Management / References: Atif |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

The initiative delivered a 9x spike in appreciation messages becoming the highest annual recognition peak on their platform.  3) Boss Appreciation Day – Bottom-Up Recognition Campaign To encourage upward and multi-directional appreciation, a large enterprise conducted a focused one-week campaign encouraging employees to recognize their managers and supervisors.  Badges such as “Team-First Visionary,” “Mentor Marvel,” and “Feedback Guru” drove a noticeable rise in upward appreciation and boosted cross-level engagement on the social feed. One of our large global Pharma clients went on record saying that this campaign set off a more sustained trend of employees recognising their supervisors and leaders to the extent that they have not needed to run this campaign again!  4) Seasonal & Culture Moments Campaigns Across Multiple Clients Many organizations activate short-term campaigns tied to cultural moments and global observances. Popular examples include: a) Earth Day – Sustainability and eco-action badges International Friendship Day – Peer bonding and collaboration badges b) World Gratitude Day – Gratitude challenges and appreciation threads c) Employee Appreciation Day – Company-wide recognition bursts d) Fun at Work Day – Creativity and team-spirited badges e) World Health Day – Wellbeing and healthy-habits recognitions  These time-bound campaigns consistently generate high, concentrated bursts of participation, helping teams reconnect, celebrate shared values, and energize the workplace culture. |  | Program Success Management / References: Atif |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 4.164 | Does your platform have the capability to support temporary recognition campaigns, such as quarterly contests, seasonal awards, or other time-bound initiatives? Please describe: How you support platform scalability for rapid growth or seasonal spikes in usage. | Yes, the platform fully supports temporary, time-bound recognition campaigns including quarterly contests, seasonal awards, and other short-duration initiatives  To support platform scalability - both for rapid growth and seasonal spikes - our approach includes several layers of proactive and reactive measures:  Regular Performance & Load Testing: We continuously conduct performance, stress, and load testing to understand system thresholds, identify bottlenecks early, and ensure the platform can handle projected traffic surges. Horizontal Scaling with Load Balancing: Traffic is distributed through a load balancer, which routes user requests across multiple droplets. This architecture allows us to scale horizontally by adding or removing droplets as demand fluctuates, ensuring seamless performance during peak periods. Real-Time Infrastructure Monitoring & Alerts: We have monitoring, observability and alerting in place for critical metrics such as CPU, memory, disk I/O, and network throughput. When resource usage spikes, alerts are triggered, giving the team time to provision additional droplets and attach them to the load balancer before performance is affected. Automated or Rapid Elastic Scaling: We leverage automated scaling policies or rapid provisioning to quickly add capacity during high-traffic events. This helps maintain stability without manual intervention. Resilient Architecture & Redundancy: Our infrastructure is designed for high availability, with redundancy at key layers, ensuring the platform remains stable even during sudden increases in traffic. |  | Program Success Management / References: Atif |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 4.167 | Please describe how your platform defines and tracks effective recognition across different teams or roles: What criteria or metrics do you use to identify ‘good’ recognition practices? | Our platform defines effective recognition as recognition that is timely, specific, values-aligned, socially reinforced, and delivered consistently across teams and roles. We track effectiveness through a combination of behavioural signals, message quality indicators, and AIRe-aligned criteria. Criteria Used to Identify ‘Good’ Recognition Practices: 1. Timeliness: Recognition given close to the contribution, not weeks later. Tracked via: post timestamps, peer vs. manager patterns. 2. Specificity & Message Quality: High-quality recognition is detailed, behaviour-linked, and >100 characters. Our analysis of 350,000+ posts shows longer, specific messages generate ~3× more engagement and drive stronger behavioural reinforcement. Supported by: Recognition Guide, message scoring, prompts to add detail. 3. Values & Behaviour Alignment: Recognition should reinforce company values and strategic priorities. Measured through: •	#tags selected during recognition •	distribution of recognitions mapped to each value •	multi-value tagging when multiple behaviours are demonstrated 4. Fairness & Coverage: Healthy recognition cultures show broad participation, not concentration in a few teams. Measured through: •	% employees recognised and % employees giving recognition •	BU-, geography-, and manager-level distribution •	equity of recognition across roles and levels 5. Social Reinforcement: Recognition with strong peer validation has higher emotional impact. Measured via: likes, comments, visibility patterns (e.g., evening/night posts get 1.2–2× more engagement). 6. Consistency Over Time: Good recognition is sustained, not episodic. Measured through: frequency per employee, per manager, per BU, month-on-month patterns. 7. Behaviour-Based Reinforcement: Profile Badges identify employees who demonstrate values consistently and highlight behaviour patterns across teams. SkillScape uses #tag and badge data to track emerging strengths and cultural hotspots. ________________________________________ How We Track Effective Recognition Across Teams / Roles: •	Giver/receiver coverage by BU, manager, geography, and role •	Recognition frequency & mix (peer appreciation vs. nominations) •	Message quality scores & average character length •	Values/#tag distribution across teams •	Profile Badge achievements and consistency indicators •	Engagement on posts (likes/comments) •	Leader and manager adoption patterns •	Recognition activity vs. team performance or morale indicators (where available) Together, these criteria and metrics give leaders a clear view of where recognition is healthy, where behaviours are being reinforced effectively, and where targeted coaching or enablement may be needed. |  | Benchmarking: Saurabh |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 4.168 | Please describe how your platform defines and tracks effective recognition across different teams or roles: How do you tailor recognition standards to accommodate differences in team functions, roles, or business units? | We tailor recognition standards across functions, roles, and business units by using a Core + Custom design approach that ensures enterprise consistency while allowing each team to reflect its unique operating context, behavioural expectations, and work realities. 1. Core (Enterprise-Wide) Standards The global framework—values, #tag structure, governance, behavioural language, and AIRe principles—remains consistent for everyone. This preserves fairness, brand identity, and cultural alignment across the organisation. 2. Customization for Teams, Roles, and BUs Each function or BU can configure recognition to reflect its specific context: •	Custom award names and criteria mapped to functional realities (e.g., risk, service, technology, operations). •	Different behavioural examples linked to each value, so teams see what the value looks like in their work (e.g., customer impact in a BFSI function vs. an IT-ITES captive center). •	BU-level campaigns around strategic themes (innovation month, customer excellence week, operational efficiency drives). •	Role-sensitive guidance for frontline, support, leadership, and specialist roles. 3. Values-Linked #Tags to Standardize What “Good” Looks Like #Tags are universal across the organisation, but each BU can define role-specific behavioural examples under each tag. This ensures: •	The standards remain global •	The interpretation becomes local and relatable This is especially important in diverse setups (e.g., India/Philippines delivery centers vs. global BFSI functions). 4. Behaviour Visibility Through Profile Badges Profile Badges allow each team to see which behaviours are consistently demonstrated within their context. They create fair, role-relevant behavioural identity signals without changing the core values. 5. SkillScape for Functional Behaviour Insights SkillScape maps strengths and behaviour clusters across functions, helping leaders see what “excellence” looks like in different teams and where reinforcement is needed. This helps tailor expectations for: •	Technical roles •	Client-facing teams •	Risk/compliance •	Shared services/captive centers •	Leadership pipelines 6. Manager Enablement & Training Programs like Modern Recognition, Ignite, and Elevate help managers understand: •	How values show up differently across functions •	How to spot meaningful contributions in each role •	How to adapt recognition standards while staying aligned to the global framework 7. Governance to Keep Customization in Check Program administrators can configure BU-level rules, but all custom elements remain anchored to the global structure to avoid fragmentation.  In summary, we use one global framework (values, #tags, AIRe), enhanced with BU-, role-, and function-specific interpretations, examples, badges, and campaigns—ensuring recognition feels relevant to each team without losing the integrity of the enterprise program. |  | Benchmarking: Saurabh |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Fair, Simple Award Decisioning + Boost: While workflows allow differentiated award values, we recommend single-value awards to reduce decision burden for managers. To recognise exceptional work, leaders can use Boost, adding extra points on top of a manager’s recognition. Intelligent Insights (SkillScape & Behaviour Analytics): SkillScape and behaviour-linked analytics help managers see emerging strengths, values demonstrated, and pockets of excellence within their teams—showing them why recognition matters and who deserves it based on actual behavioural signals. | 4.173 | Please describe how your recognition platform has evolved over the past five years. Include the key drivers of change—such as client feedback, market trends, technology advancements, or shifts in workforce expectations—and explain how these changes have improved platform effectiveness, engagement, or scalability. | Recognition Platform Evolution Over the Past Five Years Over the past five years, our recognition platform has evolved significantly, transforming from a traditional rewards mechanism into a modern, intelligent recognition ecosystem anchored in behavioural science and designed for global scale. This evolution has been shaped by client feedback, market trends, technology advancements, and shifting workforce expectations. Client Feedback: Client insights have driven major advancements in usability, relevance, and impact. Improvements such as streamlined award workflows, mobile-first experiences, real-time peer recognition, value-linked award structures, and enhanced governance controls were all shaped by feedback from large, distributed enterprises. As clients sought greater strategic alignment, we progressively embedded organisational values, behavioural prompts, and richer analytics across the platform. Market Trends: Hybrid and global workforces created a need for digital, social, and inclusive recognition experiences. We responded with enhanced mobile capabilities, social feeds, cross-team visibility, and localisation features that allow global consistency with local nuance. These changes helped improve participation and cultural cohesion across regions and employee types. Technology Advancements: Advancements in AI, data engineering, and event-driven architecture have reshaped how recognition is delivered, analysed, and reinforced. We introduced: • AI-powered Recognition Guide for message-quality scoring and improvement prompts • Intelligent nudges to encourage equitable and timely recognition • Predictive insights that help identify recognition gaps or emerging behavioural patterns • Deep analytics for team-level and BU-level cultural indicators Our cloud-native architecture now supports enterprise-grade scalability across geographies, with seamless integration into major HRIS, LMS, and performance systems. Workforce Shifts: Younger employees expect recognition to be real-time, social, values-driven, and purpose-aligned. We expanded features around peer-to-peer appreciation, social visibility, gamification, and manager enablement to meet these expectations. This shift made recognition more participative and embedded into daily routines.  A Major Step Forward: The AIRᵉ Framework A foundational milestone in the platform’s evolution was the creation of the AIRᵉ framework. Seeing the absence of a structured, quantifiable methodology to guide recognition program design, our Centre of Excellence analysed 150+ global programs and validated themes against behavioural science. AIRᵉ now underpins every aspect of our platform — from award structures and nudges to analytics, audits, and roadmap priorities. Today, AIRᵉ is undergoing academic validation through our research partnership with the University of Liverpool.  Recent and Upcoming Enhancements (Intelligent Recognition Roadmap) Building on AIRᵉ, we have expanded into behavioural intelligence, designing features that turn recognition into meaningful insights for performance, capability building, and culture management. Recognition Roll A personalised “year-in-review” narrative for each employee, showcasing: • Values demonstrated most consistently • Behaviours they are known for • Signature accomplishments recognised across teams This strengthens development conversations and embeds recognition into performance storytelling. SkillScape A behavioural capability map that shows where core values and behaviours are strongest across teams, functions, and geographies. This helps leaders: • Identify behaviour hotspots • Pinpoint emerging talent • Detect capability gaps • Support succession and workforce planning Advanced Campaign Management The platform now supports more sophisticated campaign creation, targeting, localisation, and automation — helping organisations drive year-round engagement instead of episodic spikes. Recognition Intelligence Enhancements Recent and upcoming improvements include: • Context-aware nudges for managers • Deeper value and #tag analytics • Leadership visibility tools for recognition equity • Advanced filters that help employees find and celebrate important contributions • Progressive AI improvements to message refinement and recognition guidance These roadmap features move recognition from being an engagement driver to a behaviour intelligence layer that informs performance, leadership development, and culture strategy.  Impact of These Enhancements Together, these improvements have made the platform more: • Effective — with stronger behavioural reinforcement and value alignment • Engaging — with mobile-first access, social visibility, and intelligent nudges • Scalable — with cloud-native architecture and enterprise integrations • Insightful — with recognition data serving talent, culture, and leadership decisions • Future-ready — with roadmap features that continue to evolve alongside workforce expectations  Summary In summary, our platform has evolved into a modern, intelligent, behaviour-led recognition ecosystem powered by AIRᵉ and strengthened by advanced analytics, AI augmentation, and continuous innovation. These enhancements ensure that recognition is meaningful, equitable, scalable, and tightly aligned to performance, development, and culture-building for large global enterprises. |  | Program Success Management / References: Atif |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 5.3 | Please describe the methods and metrics your organization uses to evaluate the effectiveness of client recognition programs. Specifically, include how you define successful recognition, the KPIs you track, and how these insights are used to improve program outcomes. | We evaluate recognition program effectiveness through a comprehensive, behaviour-focused measurement model that integrates our AIRᵉ Framework (Appreciation, Incentivization, Reinforcement, Emotional Connect) and our Return on Expectations (ROE) methodology. We define successful recognition as recognition that is frequent, meaningful, values-aligned, equitable, timely, and tied to both cultural and business outcomes. Our measurement approach assesses both early activation and long-term behavioural and organisational impact.  Our evaluation spans four dimensions: adoption, behaviour, sentiment, and outcomes. Adoption metrics include unique logins, percentage of employees giving and receiving recognition, recognition frequency, peer-versus-manager recognition patterns, mobile adoption across distributed and frontline roles, cross-team recognition flow, and monetary redemption activity. Redemption-related KPIs include redemption rates, time-to-redeem, catalogue preferences, and budget utilisation patterns—critical indicators of perceived fairness, accessibility, and motivational effectiveness under the Incentivization pillar of AIRᵉ.  Behavioural metrics assess whether recognition reinforces the values and behaviours the organisation expects. These include value tagging, message-quality indicators, manager participation quality, and Profile Badge attainment, which measures repeat and consistent demonstration of desired behaviours, values, and skills over time. Badge progression is a key indicator that recognition is driving habit formation rather than one-off transactions, directly strengthening Reinforcement and Emotional Connect.  Sentiment and experience are measured through CSAT, NPS, in-platform feedback, support ticket trends, manager confidence scores, and social engagement on recognition posts. Operational KPIs monitor budget usage, workflow performance, catalogue fulfilment, and integration stability. Together, these reflect the authenticity, clarity, and accessibility of the recognition experience.  Outcome metrics—evaluated through our ROE methodology—assess how recognition contributes to engagement, inclusion, collaboration, leadership behaviours, discretionary effort, team climate, and indicators of manager and team effectiveness. Over time, these insights can be correlated with retention patterns, productivity signals, and adoption of desired behaviours across business units.  All KPIs are consolidated in quarterly business reviews (QBRs). Our Program Success Managers analyse adoption trends, behavioural gaps, values alignment, manager performance patterns, and friction points to recommend targeted improvements, including BU-level campaigns, workflow adjustments, enriched coaching, behavioural nudges, and communication refinements. Recognition Guide prompts, badge reinforcement, and AIRᵉ-aligned interventions are deployed in real time to shift patterns and sustain momentum.  Through this structured, data-driven model, Vantage Circle ensures recognition programs are not only widely adopted but used effectively—strengthening desired behaviours, accelerating cultural alignment, and delivering measurable, sustainable organisational impact. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal | Can we include  a. Repeat/ Consistent demonstration of behaviours/Values/ Skills etc.. as a KPI we measure and drive through profile badges  Also, can we attempt to answer this question in alignment with AIRe. Check with Saurabh |  |  | I reworked this answer. |  |  |
| 5.4 | Please attach case studies or metrics demonstrating the return on investment (ROI) or business impact of your platform for existing clients. Please include: a) Specific examples or client success stories b) Quantitative or qualitative results achieved c) The methods or metrics used to measure ROI or business impact d) Any supporting data or documentation | Vantage Circle measures recognition impact using our Return on Expectations (ROE) framework, a behavioural-science-based approach adapted from the Kirkpatrick Evaluation Model that provides a comprehensive view of culture, behaviour, leadership, and performance outcomes. ROE offers a more complete and reliable way to assess recognition impact than traditional ROI models, which often focus narrowly on financial returns; however, where clients have the data infrastructure to measure ROI (e.g., turnover, engagement, productivity trends), we support them in mapping recognition outcomes to business indicators. ROE is frequently the preferred model for large global organizations because it captures the broader impact that recognition has on culture, conduct, leadership habits, inclusion, collaboration, and employee experience. We have provided a detailed understanding of our ROE approach in the attachment: Vantage Circle POV and Framework (slides 15 -18)   Client examples include: (Please note: The client reference is used with the organization’s consent)   Tata Communications (10,000+ employees across 190+ countries), where recognition became a core enabler of their transformation from infrastructure-led to platform-led. Through AIRe and ROE, the “Applause” program evolved into a behaviour-shaping engine aligned to DRIVE Ahead transformation behaviours, resulting in stronger alignment to business-critical behaviours, improved collaboration and trust, and significant increases in recognition activity, including a 185% increase in peer-to-peer recognition, 26% rise in managerial awards, 134% increase in active users, and recognition occurring nearly every two minutes.  Wipro (250,000+ employees across 66 countries) adopted our AIRe-aligned “Winners’ Circle” framework to reinforce its 5 Habits of Culture globally, resulting in greater leadership reinforcement of desired behaviours, increased belonging and inclusion, stronger collaboration, and substantial engagement uplift. Quantitatively, Wipro achieved a 97.5% increase in peer appreciation, 550,000+ recognitions in two years, 30,000+ long-service awards, and 25,000+ unique nominators. Both programs earned Brandon Hall Gold Awards for excellence.    Our ROE model evaluates impact across four levels,namely Reaction, Learning, Behaviour, and Results using indicators such as recognition fairness, manager capability, values alignment, specificity of recognition messages, leadership reinforcement patterns, collaboration networks, engagement uplift, leadership effectiveness improvements, discretionary effort indicators, and behaviour adoption. Execution KPIs include login rates, % of employees giving and receiving recognition, recognition velocity, message quality, budget utilization, and participation across business units and geographies.    To support ongoing governance, Vantage Circle provides AIRe Assessment Reports, quarterly KPI dashboards, annual recognition audits, global and country-level AIRe reports, GPTW R&R scorecards, case studies, and year-over-year ROE tracking. This enables clients to monitor culture, leadership habits, behavioural adoption, and performance indicators over time. Overall, ROE provides Wells Fargo with a disciplined, evidence-based framework that links recognition to meaningful cultural and performance outcomes, offering a strategic and credible alternative to narrow, purely financial ROI calculations. |  | Benchmarking: Saurabh |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 5.5 | How will your platform provide usage analytics to identify low-engagement areas and recommend interventions? | All the main business stakeholders (program admins) have access to an updated view of recognition activity across different geographies, departments, non-monetary, monetary awards given, likes, comments, number of active employees, active managers, employees recognized, top awarding managers at the click of a button. These metrics are refreshed daily and can be zoomed in/out in an interactive and infographic representation.  All managers of the organization have an Insights dashboard (refreshed everyday) that shows the view of recognition activity under them. It shows details about who on the team was recognized when and how many days since their last recognition. Manager Insights dashboard also showcases the intra-team recognition map, charts showing recognition distribution over any given period of time. If you have multiple managers under you, the insights dashboard also shows the Recognition insights under each of your managers.  Apart from above, whenever is on the platform - there are app nudges, reminder emails reminding the user to recognise his peer/team members. We setup biweekly reminders to updated manager/budget holders on budget available and to be utilized (before it expires). Some of these nudges are also available on our MS Teams app.  HRBPs have acecss to dashboards and reports specific to their respective departments, business units.  Dashboards include data about • Highlights • Engagement • Recognition Activity  •Device-wise Behavior You can refine the data in each category using filters for country, department, and time frame for more accurate analysis.   Highlights  This section provides detailed insights into employee engagement on the platform. It includes the following:   Comparative Analysis: Recognitions made in the platform in the selected period in comparison to the last period. The total recognitions are further broken down into peer-to-peer, manager-to-peer, and cross-team recognitions.   Feed Score Timeline: Timeline view of the organizational feed score versus the benchmark.  Sentiment Analysis on Feed: This section classifies the sentiment of textual interactions on the platform into positive, negative, and neutral categories.  Geography-wise heat map: The map visualizes recognitions and points rewarded across different geographical regions, showing recognition trends within the selected time frame.  Top Values: Identifies the organizational values that employees were most frequently recognized for.  Timeline View of Engagement by Type (Non-Monetary, Monetary, and Greetings) Select between Badges/Awards/Greetings from the dropdown for a timeline view of the number of badges, awards, or greetings (according to selection) along with the number of likes, comments, and shares made on such posts in the selected time frame.  Top Awards: A chart and timeline map showing the most received Monetary awards, Non-monetary awards, and Greetings within the selected time frame   Engagement  This section provides a comprehensive overview of recognition activities across the organization, detailing the total number of recognitions made by managers, including both monetary and non-monetary awards. It covers key metrics such as total points awarded and the aggregate value of all awards, offering valuable insights into how recognition is distributed across teams and departments (set filter by department, country, and date).   Manager-Specific Recognition Activity: A tabular view displaying individual managers’ recognition activities. This data can be sorted by the number of awards given, allowing you to assess each manager’s contributions to the recognition program and monitor their impact on employee engagement.   Recognition Activity  This section provides a comprehensive analysis of recognition-related feed posts and their engagement. It offers key insights into the visibility and impact of recognitions made on the platform, including the total impressions each post has received, reflecting the reach of the recognitions.   The table presents detailed information about each recognition post, allowing you to assess various performance metrics. You can analyze the data based on the following columns:   Rank: Performance ranking of the post based on engagement metrics.  Published: The date and time the recognition post was published.  Post: Badges and Awards icon.  Citation: Recognition message.  Post Type: Type of recognition content (e.g., badge, award, greeting).  Posted By: The individual who has given the recognition.  Likes: Number of likes the post received from users.  Comments: Number of comments made on the post.  Shares: Total number of shares the post received.   Device-wise Behavior This section shows the total number of user-generated awards across devices like mobile apps and web apps, based on selected filters. This metric excludes awards from CSV uploads and system-generated sources, providing insights into how users engage with recognition activities on different devices  Reports include Employee Points Report, Appreciation Report, Points Redemption Report, Award Nomination Status Report, Budget Allocation Report and Budget Utilization Report, Engagement Statitics Report, Milestone Redemption Report. Reports are extremely customizable and can be tweaked to include information captured in the workflow.  We provide Quarterly Business Review (QBR) reports highlighting platform usage. These reports offer insights into user engagement and help in identifying areas for improvement. This report includes facets such as login rate or platform adoption rate covering the total logins, unique logins for the entire quarter; monetary and non-monetary awards given/received per user; Business Units/ Managers where budget utilization is low or under utilized.   The above different mechanisms, tools and reports help in understanding each engagement area and adopting approach to improve the program and user experience. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal | Can we reconstruct this answer to say we provide a variety of analytics to key program stakeholders on low engagement areas such as  a. | 5.6 | Please describe your standard reporting solution. In your response, include: Who has access to reporting within your platform (e.g., administrators, managers, employees). | Our platform offers a comprehensive, scalable, and data-rich reporting solution designed to provide complete visibility into all Rewards & Recognition (R&R) activities. Reports are refreshed nightly (midnight data indexing) to ensure accuracy across all dashboards and downloadable datasets. Administrators can apply advanced filters such as Country, Department, and custom Date Range to drill down into insights at a granular level. Access to Reporting  We provide controlled, role-based access to ensure secure and relevant data visibility: • Super Admins Have full access to the complete reporting suite, including all organization-wide reports and financial/budget reports. • HR Admins Have restricted access based on the departments assigned to them. They can view and download reports only for their mapped departments, ensuring appropriate data governance. • Managers Have access to their teams insights, dashboards depicting budget utilization, charts and heatmaps about recognition activity within and outside their team. Manager of managers can have a view of full umbrella and activity under their portfolio. • Employees Details about any recognition activity they executed or were part of, points statement, redemptions history.  Available Reports in the Platform Employee-Centric Reports • Employee Points Report – Overview of all monetary reward points awarded to employees. • Appreciation Report – Summary of non-monetary recognitions received by employees. • Points Redemption Report – Details of all monetary reward redemptions. • Profile Badge Report – Overview of badges earned by employees.  Budget & Finance Reports • Budget Allocation Report – Details of budgets allocated to budget holders. • Budget Utilization Report – Insights into budgets spent by budget holders. • Budget Transaction Report – Complete record of allocation, utilization, and transfer activities. • Purchased Budget Report – Summary of all budget purchase transactions. • Budget Transfer Report – Details of budget transfers between holders.  Award & Nomination Reports • Award Nomination Status Report – Summary of nominations and their approval statuses. • Panel Nominations Report – Insights into panel-submitted nominations.  CSV & Bulk Upload Reports • CSV Rewards Upload Report – Record of monetary and non-monetary recognitions uploaded via CSV.  New (Beta) Reports • Budget Allocation/Deallocation Transactions Report (Beta) – Detailed allocation/deallocation activities. • Budget Utilization Transactions Report (Beta) – Comprehensive utilization-level insights. • Budget Balance Consolidated Report (Beta) – Consolidated view of budget balances across holders.  Miscellaneous Reports • Transaction Report – End-to-end view of all reward-related transactions. |  |  | Why employees have access to no reports ? | 5.9 | Please attach examples of recognition practices implemented through your platform that have led to measurable improvements in employee retention, morale, performance, or organizational culture. Please include: a) Specific recognition initiatives or programs b) The metrics or methods used to measure outcomes c) Quantitative or qualitative results demonstrating impact d) Any case studies or client success stories that illustrate these improvements | We support organizations with targeted recognition practices that boost participation, reinforce desired behaviours, and strengthen culture. Below are examples of initiatives implemented through our platform and the measurable outcomes they delivered.  a) Recognition Practices / Programs  1. Thematic Campaigns Time-bound campaigns with custom badges and messaging used to amplify recognition during key moments or to reinforce specific behaviours. 2. Profile Badges (Behaviour-Signalling Badges) Always-on, values-linked badges earned through recognition activity. These promote consistency, social reinforcement, and visible behavioural identity. 3. Data-Informed Prompts & Message Quality Features Analysis of 350,000+ recognition posts revealed that: •	Posts after 6 PM receive 1.2–2× higher engagement •	Messages 100+ characters get ~3× more likes/comments •	Peer appreciations outperform nominations These insights shaped features like Recognition Guide, richer message prompts, and scheduling nudges.  b) Metrics Used to Measure Outcomes •	Change in peer recognition volume •	Badge usage and campaign participation •	Average recognition moments per employee •	Post engagement (likes/comments) •	Appreciation uplift after Profile Badge activation •	Values/ #tag alignment •	BU- and geography-level adoption trends •	Attrition analysis for employees receiving regular recognition versus that do not •	Qualitative feedback on morale and culture  c) Quantitative & Qualitative Results  • Overall analysis of attrition vis. recognition given Deep dive analysis for a client in the Pharma sector revealed the following:  - ~66% of exits came from employees with 4 or fewer recognition touchpoints in the prior 12 months.​  - 1 in 5 leavers received no recognition at all in the year before they left.​  - Only 13% of leavers had 10 or more recognition moments in the prior year  • Campaign Example 1 (Women’s Day) Month-long themed campaign using “HERo” badges. Impact:  - 2× increase in peer-to-peer recognitions  - Higher visibility for stories of women across levels  • Campaign Example 2 (Men’s Day / Movember) Short-duration celebration using thematic badges. Impact:  - 9× spike in appreciation messages  - Highest recognition peak of the year   • Profile Badge Activation Across Multiple Clients Across several global and regional enterprises:  - Appreciation rates increased 30%–115% within months  - One large engineering center saw recognitions rise from ~1,400 to ~10,000 over six months  - Badge visibility created healthy competition and consistent behaviour reinforcement Collectively, these improvements supported higher morale, better message quality, and stronger alignment to organizational values.  d) Supporting Data & Documentation We provide: •	Campaign impact dashboards •	Profile Badge analytics •	Insights from analysing 350,000+ recognition posts •	AIRe Assessment Reports linking behaviours to design quality •	Annual Program Audits with year-over-year behavioural movement •	Case studies (anonymous or name-disclosed as required) We have provided examples of this analysis and insights in the attachment: Vantage Circle POV and Framework (slides 19-24)  Our data-led approach ensures recognition practices evolve based on real behavioural insights. Features such as Recognition Guide, #tag mapping, Profile Badges, and the emerging SkillScape solution stem directly from platform analytics—continuously strengthening culture, morale, and behaviour adoption. |  | Benchmarking: Saurabh |  |  |  |  |  |  |

The platform does not calculate or withhold taxes, but it ensures that award activity is clearly tagged and reportable so that Wells Fargo can manage all downstream IRS or fringe benefit requirements through its internal processes or third-party systems. |  | John & Nikhil |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Example: Wipro Ireland Gift Card Compliance Workflow A recent example demonstrates how Vantage Circle adapts to country-specific tax obligations. Irish tax regulations require that certain gift card transactions be reported to tax authorities before activation. To support this requirement, Vantage Circle worked with the client to redesign the redemption workflow by: • Introducing a delayed activation window after redemption • Updating employee-facing screens and email notifications to explain the delay • Restricting gift cards to only those compliant with Irish reporting rules • Providing structured redemption reports to support the employer’s manual tax filing process  Under this model, employees redeem a gift card and receive an immediate confirmation, but activation occurs only after the employer has completed their reporting. This ensured full compliance while maintaining a clear and positive employee experience.  Other Client Use Cases Across global programs, clients commonly use platform capabilities to support local compliance, including: • Defining taxable and non-taxable award classifications by country • Setting issuance or redemption thresholds based on local rules (for example, de minimis limits) • Using transaction-level exports to support W-2, 1099, T4A, benefit-in-kind, or perquisite reporting • Applying entity-level financial controls for multi-jurisdictional programs These features help organizations operationalize tax treatment consistently across diverse geographies.  Recommended Best Practices Based on experience across large multinational clients, recommended practices include: • Aligning HR, Payroll, Finance, and Tax teams during initial configuration • Clearly defining tax classifications and award rules by country or entity • Establishing internal review cycles to validate thresholds and compliance logic • Using structured exports to feed payroll or tax systems rather than relying on manual interpretation • Engaging a global tax advisory partner to validate configurations and ensure consistency across jurisdictions  Platform Limitations Vantage Circle does not interpret tax law, calculate taxes, or perform statutory filings. | 6.28 | Please describe how your platform’s pricing model—specifically, billing on issuance versus billing on redemption—affects the ability to accurately track and report on taxable versus non-taxable awards. In your response, address the following:  Tracking Mechanisms: How does each billing model (issuance vs. redemption) impact your system’s ability to distinguish, track, and report taxable and non-taxable awards at the time of award, at the time of redemption, and for year-end reporting? | Our platform supports both billing on issuance and billing on redemption, and allows these models to coexist across different program types so that each program can be configured for the best fit with tax compliance and accounting practices.  In US specifically, which is a significant majority of the global headcount, IRS rules create a unique opportunity for a dual billing model to co-exist to avail policy benefits.   Heres' how the billing model impacts tax tracking in the Vantage Circle platform, with a US context for example.  For points‑based performance recognition programs, billing on issuance is the recommended approach. In these programs, the taxable event is typically tied to the employee receiving points or a monetary-equivalent award, and billing on issuance aligns the invoice, the recognition event, and the tax reporting trigger. This enables finance and payroll teams to treat issued value as taxable (or non‑taxable, if applicable) in near real time, without waiting for future redemptions.  For service award programs that are intended to qualify as non‑taxable under IRS (and similar) rules, billing on redemption is generally more appropriate. The IRS criteria for non‑taxable years‑of‑service awards depend on the actual item received and its fair market value (FMV), along with conditions such as:  a. The award being a tangible item (not cash or cash‑equivalent) b. The value limits (for example, 400 USD or 1,600 USD depending on plan registration and applicable policy) c. Minimum 5‑year service intervals and a formal presentation  These conditions can only be verified once the employee has chosen and received a specific tangible product. If such programs are billed on issuance (e.g., when points or a notional balance are granted), the accurate FMV is still unknown. Finance would then need to reconcile the final product and price at redemption and post payroll adjustments later, creating extra downstream work or risking non‑compliance if that step is skipped. Billing on redemption for service awards eliminates this mismatch by tying the invoice directly to the redeemed item and its confirmed FMV.  Note: A similar scenario arises in Canada where CRA manadate a similar compliance framework but with subtle difference like a CAD 500 cap on FMV.  Tracking Mechanisms:  Issuance vs Redemption vs Year‑End Regardless of billing model, the platform is designed to distinguish, track, and report taxable vs non‑taxable awards at three key points in the lifecycle:  At Time of Award (Issuance) For points‑based or immediate‑value awards, the system records: employee name , program name , award type, award category, date of issuance, award value, and the applicable billing model.  At Time of Redemption For service awards or point‑based catalogs, the system captures: product name, product description, delivered price including tax, date of redemption, milestone year/ service tenure, and applicable billing model.  For qualified years‑of‑service or similar programs, redemption data is used to confirm whether the award meets non‑taxable criteria (tangible item, FMV threshold, interval between awards). Where it fails the criteria, the system can flag the value as taxable for later payroll inclusion. Under billing on redemption, this is also the point where the invoiced amount and the taxable/non‑taxable classification are aligned.  For Year‑End Reporting Under the Admin Panel, the reporting and analytics engine includes a report builder that allows admins to select and combine all relevant data fields (issuance and redemption events) across programs and billing models.  For service award programs, common fields include: employee, product name, product description, FMV/price including tax, milestone year, date of redemption, and a taxable/non‑taxable flag.  For performance/points programs, typical fields include: employee, date of issuance, award value issued, award name, award category, program type, and taxable/non‑taxable status.  The platform can aggregate data by employee, program, or billing model so that clients can generate a single consolidated file for payroll and year‑end tax reporting (e.g., taxable totals per employee, separated from non‑taxable service awards).  Impact of Billing Model on Reporting Accuracy Because all tax‑relevant fields are captured at both issuance and redemption, there is no loss of tracking or reporting capability under either billing model. What changes is the timing and source of “final” FMV and tax classification:  Under billing on issuance, reports primarily use issuance data (award value at the time of grant), which is ideal for cash/near‑cash and points‑based performance recognition.  Under billing on redemption, reports rely on redemption data (actual item and FMV), which is ideal for years‑of‑service and other qualified award programs where non‑taxable treatment depends on the redeemed item.  In practice, this means client admins can mix and match: for example, run points‑based performance programs on billing‑on‑issuance and years‑of‑service programs on billing‑on‑redemption, while still rolling everything up into a unified taxable vs non‑taxable view at year‑end. |  | Nikhil |  |  |  |  |  | true |

In your response, address the following:  Data Availability: What data fields and reporting capabilities are available to support compliance with IRS and other regulatory requirements for taxable awards under each billing model? | As a platform that allows for both billing models to co-exist, essential fields required for tax accounting of either model are available. Our Report Builder functionality allows Admins to create custom reports by program or program type.  We also have the ability to create a custom (ready to download) report that can be auto triggered to different accounting teams in different geographies on a periodic basis.    Here are the data fields available in alignment with either billing model :  For Programs billed on Issuance  a. Employee identifier (name, email ID) b. | 6.30 | Please describe how your platform’s pricing model—specifically, billing on issuance versus billing on redemption—affects the ability to accurately track and report on taxable versus non-taxable awards. In your response, address the following:  Operational Implications: Are there differences in how taxable events are triggered, recorded, and reported depending on whether billing occurs at issuance or redemption? How does your platform handle scenarios where points are issued in one tax year and redeemed in another? | Our platform is designed to ensure accurate tracking and reporting of taxable and non-taxable awards under both billing on issuance and billing on redemption. The way taxable events are triggered, recorded, and reported is flexible to align with the operational and compliance requirements of each model.  For Programs Billed on Issuance Tax Event Triggered at Award Issuance i.e when points, gift cards, or monetary awards are given, the taxable event occurs immediately, aligning tax recognition, invoicing, and payroll reporting with the issuance date. At this point, the platform automatically captures key data at issuance (employee details, award value, program type, taxable/non-taxable status), and classifies each award for reporting in the current payroll tax period. For year-end reporting, all issued awards are aggregated by employees and thus there is no risk of delayed tax liability, as all recognized value is tied to the original issue date.​  For Programs biilled on Redemption Tax Event Triggered at Redemption the taxable event occurs when the award (a physical tangible item in the case of a Service Award bound by IRS rules) is selected and fulfilled. Invoicing, actual fair market value (FMV), and taxable status are set at redemption. At the point of redemption, the system registers fields such as the product’s FMV, type, and eligibility for non-taxable treatment, recording exact details for audit and reporting. Reporting is driven by redemption activity, ensuring the right value is declared for payroll/tax forms in the period the employee actually receives the benefit. If a redemption occurs in a different tax year from issuance, the platform automatically posts the transaction to the correct reporting year, minimizing reconciliation errors.​  Situations when the Tax Year Changes: When billed on Issuance, the original award value is recognized for tax purposes in the year of issuance, regardless of when points are redeemed. Unredeemed points at year-end do not trigger additional tax reporting, as the taxable event has already occurred and been recorded.  When billed on redemption, tax liability is determined at the point of redemption. If redemption occurs in a subsequent tax year, the income is reported in that calendar year, in line with local payroll requirements. The system maintains a complete life-cycle audit trail linking issuance and redemption, automatically aligning reporting to the appropriate tax year. |  | Nikhil |  |  |  |  |  | true |

| 6.33 | Please describe your platform’s approach to recognition award redemptions and breakage. Specifically:  Do you expect or retain breakage (unredeemed awards/points) as part of your program? If so, please explain your policy and practices regarding breakage. | Vantage Circle delivers all gift cards at true face value with no markups on rewards, no fulfillment fees, and zero breakage -unlocking an estimated $3–$4 million in direct, hard-dollar savings for Wells Fargo. Our Global Gift Card offering has been built on strong partnerships with best-in-class sourcing efficiency to not require adding a markup on the face value while still delivering a healthy account level EBIDTA.  100% of our client accounts benefit from this sourcing efficiency with 0 fees on top of gift card face value being a standard offering. ​  We do not retain breakage from unredeemed awards/ points as points never expire at Vantage Circle. Following is a process we follow to address the following scenarios  a. For Termed Employees for a points based program that is billed on issuance, if the separation is voluntary, reminder notifications are sent via the system to nudge the departing employee to redeem any accumulated points before leaving. If there are still any unredeemed points, we issue a default digital gift card (Visa/Mastercard) loaded with the points balance and send to such employee. For all such cases, we charge a flat 6.5% of the loaded balance amount as a service fee to manage the deliverable and supporting documentation. At an 14% average unredeemed points last year across all enterprise clients, the fee on all default gifts computed to 6.5%x14% = roughly 1% of the unredeemed points unlike vendors that retain all unredeemed points billed on issuance to make 5-8% in breakage value.  b. For employer triggered (involuntary) separations, we follow the same process and issue the default digital gift card loaded with the unredeemed balance + 6.5% to the company for them to deliver to the departed employee.  c. For termed employees who are eligible for a service award, we leave the option to the employer to decide how they would like us to treat such cases. As taxation hasn't occured, it is not mandatory to deliver the service award. For programs like service awards that are billed on redemption there is naturally no scope to retain breakage. |  | Nikhil |  |  |  |  |  | true |

| 6.58 | Describe how your platform manages product lifecycle updates. How are new products introduced, deprecated, or replaced across global catalogs? | Our platform uses a proactive, continuous lifecycle management process to ensure that our global catalog - featuring hundreds of thousands of curated items and access to millions through our supplier network - remains current, relevant, and high-quality across all regions. We treat the catalog as a dynamic, market-driven asset and manage it through three core pillars: Introduction, Maintenance, and Deprecation.  1. Product Introduction and Catalog Expansion  New product introduction is driven through structured supplier collaboration and ongoing market research.  Continuous Supplier Engagement: We maintain regular product review sessions with our in-country suppliers to understand upcoming launches, seasonal assortments, roadmap updates, and category expansions. This ensures we are among the earliest to introduce relevant items into the catalog.  Active Market Research & Sourcing: Our curation and category management teams continually evaluate emerging trends, innovative product categories, and local/regional vendors. This includes trade show participation, competitor analysis, and targeted sourcing to fill any geographical or category-specific gaps.  Trend-Led Strategic Curation: Trend analysis across consumer gifting behavior, corporate gifting needs, and regional preferences informs our curation strategy. For example, increased global interest in sustainable gifting triggers immediate sourcing and onboarding of eco-conscious brands and products.  2. Product Maintenance and Optimization  Mid-lifecycle management ensures products remain accurate, up-to-date, and aligned with market expectations.  Performance & Inventory Monitoring: We monitor product performance across metrics such as conversion, customer satisfaction, and inventory levels from all supplier locations to maintain a healthy, high-performing catalog.  Technology & Relevance Governance: Category managers review product relevance continuously, especially in technology and lifestyle categories. Outdated models, legacy versions, or items no longer offered by premier brands are flagged for removal and replaced with newer alternatives. Exceptions are made only when the brand itself continues to support or market a prior-generation model.  3. Product Deprecation and Global Replacement  End-of-life (EOL) management is executed in collaboration with suppliers to maintain catalog continuity.  Supplier-Driven Deprecation: When a supplier designates a product as EOL, we execute a structured replacement workflow. This includes identifying an equivalent item from the same supplier or from an alternative vetted vendor based on price, function, style, and local availability.  Systemic Global Replacement: Deprecated products are removed across all global catalog instances.  They are suppressed from search results, recommendations, and active workflows.  For any programs actively using the item, we identify a suitable alternative to avoid user disruption.  When applicable, a short grace period is applied to allow fulfilment using remaining on-hand inventory; after this period, the product is permanently archived.  This continuous, data-driven lifecycle management approach ensures that our global catalogs remain fresh, relevant, and aligned with current-year market availability- delivering a consistently high-quality reward experience across all regions. |  | Snappy |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 6.62 | Please describe: How your invoicing system documents and itemizes charges by employee and AU. | Our invoicing framework is designed to give Finance teams complete clarity into how every reward-related charge is attributed and billed. Each employee is mapped within the platform to their corresponding department, legal entity, country, and Accounting Unit (AU). This ensures that every transaction carries the correct financial ownership from the moment it occurs.  When an employee redeems reward points, the system automatically generates a transaction record in our database with key attributes, including:  - Employee details - Assigned AU / department / entity - Reward selected - Cost of the reward - Shipping charges and taxes (if applicable) - Date and time of redemption  These attributes form the basis of our billing logic.  Our reporting engine is configured to extract and group transactions according to your financial structure. Finance teams can receive data filtered by AU, entity, department, country, or any combination of these fields. This allows us to produce invoices that clearly reflect the actual reward spend for each financial owner, with full employee-level detail for audit and chargeback purposes.  The result is a clean, auditable invoice package that:  Itemizes all charges per employee and per AU  Includes detailed line items (points-based awards, merchandise costs, shipping, taxes)  Ensures accurate chargeback and reconciliation across complex multi-entity structures  This structured approach will allow Wells Fargo to maintain precise financial control while ensuring billing aligns seamlessly to your internal accounting and validation processes. |  | Vijay/Prashansa |  |  |  |  |  |  |

Specifically, explain how the program is adapted or optimized for different geographies to ensure relevance, inclusivity, and value for all employees regardless of location. | Our platform is designed to run global recognition programs that can be tailored at both country and global levels. | 8.2 | Describe your capabilities for producing and distributing physical collateral across Wells Fargo’s global regions. Specifically, how do you leverage local fulfillment partners or in-region production facilities to eliminate or minimize customs delays, import taxes, and international shipping costs? Please include details on your logistics workflows, compliance with local regulations, and any technology platforms used to manage regional inventory and fulfillment. | Our physical reward fulfilment model is built entirely on in-country sourcing and distribution, ensuring reliable delivery across all Wells Fargo global regions while eliminating cross-border friction. All physical collateral - whether merchandise or packaged rewards - is produced, warehoused, and shipped within the recipient’s own country or region, following our integrated fulfilment model.  Local Fulfilment Partners & In-Region Production We leverage vetted local fulfilment partners in every supported country. These partners manage: • Domestic sourcing and production • Local warehousing • Pick/pack/ship services • Domestic delivery using national carrier networks  Because all items are fulfilled locally, there is no international shipping, no customs processing, and no risk of import taxes or duties. This structure removes the delays and cost exposures typically associated with cross-border logistics.  Logistics Workflows Ordering, fulfilment, and shipping workflows operate entirely within local markets: • Orders automatically route to the appropriate in-country supplier via our platform. • Suppliers produce or pick and pack the item and ship via domestic carriers. • Tracking information flows directly back into the platform for full visibility. This ensures consistent delivery timelines, localized handling, and transparent recipient updates in every region.  Compliance With Local Regulations All suppliers are required to meet local regulatory, tax, and operational requirements. By using in-market partners instead of global hubs, we ensure: • Local tax compliance • Country-specific product and safety standards • Region-appropriate merchandise and cultural relevance • Elimination of customs duties and import restrictions This approach provides compliance integrity across all regions where Wells Fargo employees are located.  Technology Platform for Regional Inventory & Fulfilment Our technology platform manages regional inventory and fulfilment through near real-time data feeds from each in-country supplier. This includes: • Live catalog updates (stock, pricing, new products) • Automated order routing to the correct country partner • Shipment status and delivery confirmations • Reporting dashboards covering fulfilment, issue rates, and performance metrics All global catalogs remain aligned with local availability and current-year product cycles, ensuring accuracy and freshness of inventory.  The only exception to this is for logo-branded/ custom items (e.g., Wells Fargo–branded joining kits, custom awards). These items are decorated on demand and fulfilled from the closest available specialized decoration facility located in India, Hong Kong, Portugal, or the United States. |  | Carlton |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 8.5 | How does your platform administer parity in awards for global markets based on Wells Fargo calculations? Please describe: The workflow for updating parity values annually or as needed, including stakeholder review and approval processes. | Our platform administers parity in awards for global markets based on Wells Fargo calculations by following a defined governance workflow for updating parity values annually - or more frequently if market conditions require it. The process begins with the collection of updated financial inputs, including exchange rates, cost-of-living indicators, and other local market factors that influence award parity. These data points are incorporated into Wells Fargo’s parity calculation methodology to generate the proposed updated values.   The preliminary parity values then move through a structured stakeholder review. This includes internal compensation and analytics teams, Wells Fargo program owners, and regional HR/Total Rewards stakeholders who validate accuracy, methodology alignment, and local market applicability. Following this collaborative review, the final parity values are submitted for formal approval through Wells Fargo’s designated governance process.   Once approved, the updated parity values are configured within the platform, tested for accuracy, and deployed to ensure award equity across all global markets. This end-to-end workflow ensures updates are timely, consistent, and fully aligned with Wells Fargo’s global parity standards. |  | Solution & Technical Queries: Hemanga |  |  |  |  |  | true |

What location will fulfill/warehouse/distribute for each country? | Vantage Circle fulfills rewards globally through a in-country drop-ship fulfillment model supported by a trusted network of local and international vendors. All rewards for the listed countries are sourced, warehoused, and delivered domestically using in-country suppliers and domestic carrier networks. We do not use cross-border shipping or centralized warehousing for name brand merchadise catalog items, which eliminates customs delays, reduces logistics cost, and ensures faster delivery.  Countries fully supported through in-country fulfillment: AU, CA, CN, FR, DE, HK, IN, IE, JP, KR, NL, NZ, PH, SG, SE, TW, TH, UK, UAE, US, VN  • Fulfilled entirely within each country • Shipped using domestic carriers • No international shipping involved  Our global supplier network is selected based on strict criteria around reliability, quality, deliverability, and alignment with our service standards. Fulfillment is managed through a combination of in-house logistics and vetted third-party providers to ensure accuracy and timely delivery across regions. For certain markets - particularly within the EU - we also leverage in-country and intra-EU regional partner warehouses to optimize delivery-performance and ensure compliance with local regulations.  For branded merchandise, we leverage a hybrid model of fulfillment. We have a network of in country decorators and fulfillers across the globe in major markets such as China, India, UK, EU, US, and Australia. The product selection is country specific. For certain programs, we recommend storing and fulfilling from a single location.  This approach ensures consistent brand quality while minimizing lead times. Once decorated, the items are shipped using the optimal route (domestic or cross-border, depending on product type and destination), ensuring reliable delivery. |  | Carlton/Snappy |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 8.31 | How will you support international reward redemption for the following countries: Australia, Canada, China, France, Germany, Hong Kong, India, Ireland, Japan, Korea, Netherlands, New Zealand, Philippines, Singapore, Sweden, Taiwan, Thailand, UK, United Arab Emirates, US, Vietnam b. How do you ensure inventory remains fresh (merchandise is produced in current year)? | Vantage Circle maintains a fresh, reliable, and locally relevant catalog through a combination of real-time supplier integrations and active category management. Our in-country supplier network provides continuous availability feeds - covering stock levels, pricing, and new SKUs - directly into our marketplace. Because all rewards are sourced and drop-shipped locally, merchandise is drawn from current-year production and is refreshed as suppliers update their assortments.  To complement this data-driven model, our dedicated category managers oversee product lifecycle standards across regions. They engage closely with suppliers to ensure the catalog reflects what is considered “current” for each category. Newness expectations differ by category, and our managers apply this nuance thoughtfully. For instance, in electronics, prior-generation models often remain active and widely purchased even after newer versions launch - similar to Apple continuing to list both AirPods 4 and AirPods Pro 3 as current products. Where this is appropriate, we maintain both versions to provide users with choice, price variation, and local market relevance.  This combined approach - real-time supplier data + expert category governance -keeps our catalog accurate, up-to-date, and aligned with actual consumer behavior across all markets. |  | Carlton/Snappy |  |  |  |  |  |  |
