| 8.38 | Are rewards in your catalog tailored to local preferences, vendors, and cultural norms? Please describe: The process for selecting and partnering with local vendors. | Our process for selecting local vendors and integrating them into our operations is focused on two main goals: ensuring they are established, reliable brands with verifiable in-country fulfillment infrastructure, and facilitating a seamless technical connection via our marketplace. I. Selection and Vetting  We apply a set of criteria during the initial selection phase to ensure a high standard of partnership: •        Brand & Market Presence: The vendor must be an Established Brand with a proven track record, market longevity, and a strong, positive customer reputation within the operating country. •        Fulfillment Infrastructure: We require In-Country Warehouse Facilities. •        Operational Excellence: The partner must demonstrate proven efficiency in inventory management, accurate order picking, and a reliable local delivery network. •        Quality & Compliance: The vendor must adhere to all local regulatory, safety, labor, and environmental standards, and possess all required product certifications.  II. Partnership Formalization (SLAs and Contracting) Formalizing the partnership involves setting clear expectations and ensuring mutual commitment to high standards: •        Service Level Agreements (SLAs): We require the vendor to accept Key Performance Indicators (KPIs) covering order fulfillment accuracy, lead time, and real-time inventory transparency. •        Data Security: The partner must comply with our comprehensive data protection policies for handling customer information and sensitive sales data. •        Risk Mitigation: We jointly develop and agree on a business continuity and risk mitigation plan to address potential local supply chain disruptions.  III. Vendor Onboarding Process  A dedicated onboarding process ensures the local vendor is fully integrated and operational: 1.        Initial Account Setup: We create a dedicated, secure vendor account within our marketplace for administrative purposes. 2.        Catalog Mapping & Upload: The vendor’s local product catalog is meticulously mapped to our platform's standards, covering aspects like pricing, standardized product descriptions, and imagery, before being uploaded 3.        Training & Testing: Vendor staff receive comprehensive training on the functions such as reporting, managing returns, and performance tracking. We conclude with a series of end-to-end simulated transactions. 4.        Go-Live & Monitoring: The vendor's cataog is activated. We then initiate intensive monitoring of all live orders and fulfillment performance during the first 30 days to ensure stable, reliable operations.  This integrated approach ensures that the local partnership is grounded in quality infrastructure and facilitated by seamless technology. |  | Vijay/Prashansha |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 8.42 | How does your platform manage inventory, shipping, and delivery—especially for international fulfillment—to ensure timely and accurate delivery of awards and products? Please describe: Your process for inventory management, including real-time tracking and visibility across global fulfillment centers. | We leverage enterprise level marketplace management software to operate our global marketplace. All suppliers feed us inventory through APIs or manual updates. Additionally, we have direct catalog and API integrations with the world's largest retailers, gift card aggregators etc. enabling us to offer products as they are available. All suppliers are contractually bound to adhering to our SLAs for order fulfillment and delivery.   The objective of our API integrations is to establish a secure, automated, bi-directional data flow between the vendor's logistics system and our Marketplace system. This replaces manual processes, which are prone to errors and delays, with real-time, reliable data exchange. We establish multiple data streams to ensure synchronized operations between the local vendor's fulfillment center and our marketplace platform. Data Flow: Vendor to MMS (Product & Asset Management) •        Data Stream Exchanged: Product Assets (copy, images, local pricing) •        Objective and Benefit: The vendor transmits their standardized product information to the MMS. This is critical to maintain up-to-date, accurate, and localized product assets (e.g., pricing, descriptions, and high-quality images) on the marketplace. Data Flow: MMS to Vendor (Order Fulfillment) •        Data Stream Exchanged: Order Data •        Objective and Benefit: When a customer places an order on the marketplace, the MMS automatically pushes the order details (SKU, quantity, customer shipping address) to the vendor's system (WMS) for immediate fulfillment processing. This ensures rapid dispatch and minimizes order entry errors. Data Flow: Vendor to MMS (Inventory Control) •        Data Stream Exchanged: Inventory Status •        Objective and Benefit: The vendor's WMS provides real-time stock levels back to the MMS. This ensures the marketplace never sells items that are out-of-stock, which is crucial for preventing customer dissatisfaction, backorders, and subsequent cancellations. Data Flow: Vendor to MMS (Post-Fulfillment Updates) •        Data Stream Exchanged: Fulfillment Status •        Objective and Benefit: Once the vendor's warehouse picks, packs, and dispatches the order, they automatically push the shipment confirmation and the associated tracking number back to the MMS. This allows for immediate communication of shipment status to the customer. •        Data Stream Exchanged: Returns/Discrepancies •        Objective and Benefit: The vendor communicates all returns, cancellations, or inventory discrepancies for necessary reconciliation, immediate processing, and efficient customer service updates. Technical Implementation •        API Standardization: We utilize standard, secure protocols to facilitate easier and faster connections. Data formats are standardized to ensure universal compatibility. •        Security Protocols: The API connection is secured using industry-standard and robust authentication methods to protect customer and proprietary data during transit. •        Testing and Validation: We conduct integration and performance testing before ""go-live." This seamless integration ensures that the local vendor's fulfillment center operates as a direct, synchronized extension of our marketplace, leveraging their in-country efficiency while maintaining centralized control and visibility. |  | Snappy |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 8.51 | Are you compliant with GDPR, CCPA, and other international data privacy laws? | 9.19 | Can your platform facilitate the following system requirement? Require all points based awards are decisioned by another manager. Nominations must be routed to the employee's direct manager for decisioning, unless the nominator is the direct manager. In that instance, it should go to the next level manager (the nominator's manager) If yes, please describe the system workflow/process to meet the requirement. | Yes, our platform can facilitate this system requirement through configurable approval workflows:  • When a points-based award nomination is submitted, the system automatically checks if the nominator is the employee’s direct manager. • If the nominator is not the direct manager, the nomination is routed directly to the employee’s direct manager for decisioning. • If the nominator is the employee’s direct manager, the system automatically routes the nomination to the next level manager (i.e., the nominator’s manager) for review and approval. • This ensures a dual-layer approval process for points-based awards, maintaining compliance and internal controls. • The entire workflow is configurable in the platform’s approval settings, allowing organizations to map their management hierarchies and define routing rules based on manager relationships. • Notifications and reminders are sent throughout the workflow to keep approvers informed and ensure timely decisioning.  This workflow design supports rigorous management oversight while simplifying the nomination and approval process to align with organizational policies. |  | Solution & Technical Queries: Hemanga |  |  |  |  |  | true |
| 9.20 | Can your platform facilitate the following system requirement? Enforce an annual maximum award points value for all employees. This workflow ensures equitable distribution of recognition points, prevents over-allocation, and maintains alignment with budget and governance controls, all managed seamlessly within the platform. |  | Solution & Technical Queries: Hemanga |  |  |  |  |  | true |

| 9.29 | Can your platform facilitate the following system requirement? Ensure employees cannot self-nominate or self- approve including while acting as a proxy for manager any recognition.. This is enforced through role-based access controls and nomination validation rules within the workflow. • Notifications and audit logs capture all proxy activities to maintain transparency and compliance.  This ensures strict segregation of duties and upholds the integrity of the recognition process across all scenarios. |  | Solution & Technical Queries: Hemanga |  |  |  |  |  | true |
| 9.30 | Can your platform facilitate the following system requirement? Identify points based nominations that are recurring (weekly, monthly, etc.)between same sender and recipient prior to routing for approval. If yes, please describe the system workflow/process to meet the requirement. | The system does not automatically identify recurring points-based nominations between the same sender and recipient prior to approval. Instead, the approval workflows and required business justifications are designed to ensure managers review the context and appropriateness of nominations, including frequency, during the decisioning process. This managerial oversight helps maintain program integrity without automated recurrence detection.  Should there be a need we can also enable alterts to system administrators to inform them about identified malpractices and highlight the repeat offenders based on previously defined criteria |  | Solution & Technical Queries: Hemanga |  |  |  |  |  | true |
| 9.31 | Can your platform facilitate the following system requirement? All nominations must allow the decision maker to raise/lower the points based award. If yes, please describe the system workflow/process to meet the requirement. | Yes, our platform allows decision makers to raise or lower the points-based award values during the approval process. Approvers have the capability to edit the award amount within the nomination workflow interface before finalizing their decision. However, to maintain financial control, a central budget is managed at the organizational level to ensure that any adjustments stay within allocated limits. This combination of flexible approval adjustments and centralized budget monitoring supports both governance and operational agility. |  | Solution & Technical Queries: Hemanga |  |  |  |  |  | true |

| 10.1 | Please describe your proposed implementation plan for the recognition platform. In your response, address:  Project Timeline: Provide a detailed timeline with key milestones, deliverables, and estimated go-live date for a company of our size. | Our implementation approach combines agile delivery, structured governance, and global program design practices developed through large-scale deployments at organizations such as Deloitte, Wipro, Bosch, and Tata Communications. For an enterprise of your scale, the typical implementation timeline is 6–9 months (28–40 weeks), depending on complexity, integrations, and the number of countries in scope.  Kickoff & Discovery (3–5 weeks): Project pre-kickoff alignment (objectives, success criteria, roles, governance). Formal project kickoff with all Wells Fargo stakeholders. Establishment of the governance structure, cadence, and communication plan. Review of existing policies, workflows, budgets, brand and compliance requirements, and initial integration scoping (Workday HCM, SSO, payroll). Initial data mapping, risk identification, and launch planning.  Design, Build & Configure (12–18 weeks): Discovery workshops and focused-group sessions across HR, Rewards, IT/HCM, Comms, Legal/Compliance, Payroll, and regional leaders. Program (re)design aligned to Wells Fargo cultural pillars and governance requirements. Design communication strategy, plan, and core message platform. Definition of award types, approval flows, budget structures, and audit requirements. Platform configuration including modules, permissions, branding, and business rules. Integration development (SSO, Workday HCM, payroll feeds, APIs) and validation cycles. Localization of workflows, communications, and reward catalogs. Iterative sprint reviews to confirm configuration and alignment.  Testing (6–8 weeks): Comprehensive functional testing, integration testing (SSO, Workday, GL/Payroll), end-to-end workflow validation, data verification, User Acceptance Testing (UAT) with global champions, and pre-production readiness checks.  Training & Change Management (4–8 weeks, overlapping Testing): Development of global and localized communication materials, admin and manager training, employee learning content, change-enablement planning, and launch campaign preparation.  Launch & Go-Live (2 weeks): Production cutover, data validation, integration activation, optional soft launch, full enterprise go-live, monitoring of adoption, budgets, redemptions, SSO activity, and structured command-center operations with real-time triage.  Hyper-care (4–8 weeks): Post-launch monitoring, issue resolution, optimization of workflows and user experience, supplemental training, data reconciliation support, and transition to BAU with ongoing Customer Success partnership.  Estimated Go-Live: For a Month 0 kickoff, a typical enterprise deployment goes live between Month 6 and Month 9 depending on global scope and integration dependencies.  If Wells Fargo wants to achieve a January 1, 2027 go-live, we recommend initiating the project between April and May 2026, allowing for a 8–9 month implementation cycle appropriate for a global enterprise of Wells Fargo’s size and complexity. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal | 1. From Mercer, resources involved at this phae include Change Management Lead and Change Management Consultant. Our partners, Mercer support continued reinforcement planning and early adoption measurement where requested.  Across all phases, Vantage Circle and Mercer together provide program strategy, design leadership, change enablement, configuration, technical delivery, analytics, and global customer success coverage. | 10.3 | Please describe your proposed implementation plan for the recognition platform. In your response, address:  Change Management: Describe your approach to driving user adoption and supporting change management throughout the rollout. | Our implementation plan is built around our Design–Define–Deliver–Discover–Digest (5D) methodology, which integrates structured change management, behaviour-building interventions, and continuous adoption support. Our communication strategy will extend beyond simply raising awareness and driving adoption of the recognition program. We will emphasize the critical behaviors and ways of working that align directly with Wells Fargo’s performance management processes and organizational goals. This new recognition program presents a valuable opportunity to reinforce and celebrate the behaviors Wells Fargo expects from its employees, thereby supporting a culture of high performance and continuous improvement.   For an organisation of Wells Fargo’s scale and complexity, the plan emphasises leadership alignment, manager capability, mobile-first access, and sustained behavioural reinforcement rather than a narrow focus on platform rollout. We begin with Design and Define, conducting a comprehensive change impact assessment across US-based BFSI functions, large India and Philippines captive centres, and all relevant business units and leadership cohorts. This includes detailed user profiling across leaders, managers, employees, and administrators, and mapping of existing workflows and current-state systems. During this phase, we co-design a change and communication strategy that aligns with Wells Fargo’s culture and internal values, AIRᵉ principles (Appreciation, Incentivization, Reinforcement, eMotional Connect), and behavioural expectations across functions and geographies, establishing a unified program identity while preserving controlled BU-level flexibility.  In Deliver, we roll out a multi-format global training and communication programme that includes leadership briefing and update communication,HR/People Manager Toolkit (presentation, talking points, and FAQs), Employee Announcement (email or script for leader video), live virtual training, on-demand videos, navigation guides, Employee User Guide, user FAQs, task-based walkthroughs, manager workshops, launch roadshows, and microlearning content. To deepen capability beyond platform navigation, we provide access to Modern Recognition (featuring Dave Ulrich and Chester Elton), Vantage Ignite for manager practice in meaningful, values-based recognition, and Vantage Elevate to support leadership-led culture reinforcement. These learning paths are supported by a comprehensive communications plan incorporating leadership cascades, BU-specific toolkits, and contextual messaging tailored to regional needs, ensuring employees experience clarity and simplicity as they transition from fragmented legacy systems.  Following go-live, the Discover and Digest phases focus on sustained adoption and behavioural reinforcement. We continuously monitor usage across geographies and teams and deploy behavioural nudges, message-quality prompts via Recognition Guide, targeted manager follow-ups, and BU-level engagement campaigns designed to replace ‘one week a year’ recognition spikes with continuous practice. Profile Badges reinforce consistency and build long-term habits. Our Vantage EDGE Program Success Managers partner closely with Wells Fargo’s HR and change teams to run quarterly campaigns, support BU-level enablement, and sequence communication waves to reinforce momentum. Early QBRs emphasise adoption, friction-point resolution, and workflow optimisation before shifting toward impact measurement and long-term programme evolution. Where major changes are required, we strongly recommend a phased approach to minimise disruption and build confidence across employee groups.  Wells Fargo can expect a unified recognition experience that replaces disjointed systems, enables mobile-first access for all employees, and drives strong manager adoption through education and behavioural nudges. Values alignment is strengthened through #tags and AIRᵉ, while simplified workflows and curated reward experiences reduce decision fatigue. Sustained engagement is delivered through recurring campaigns and systematic behavioural reinforcement. Overall, our structured change management approach ensures a smooth transition for Wells Fargo by balancing global consistency with BU-level flexibility and combining platform deployment with ongoing behavioural enablement, ultimately driving long-term cultural and programme success across all geographies. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal |  |  |  | I reformatted into paragraphs. |  |  |
| 10.4 | Please describe your proposed implementation plan for the recognition platform. In your response, address:  Success Metrics: Define the metrics and KPIs you use to measure implementation success (e.g., participation rates, engagement, milestone achievement, user satisfaction, ROI). | Vantage Circle measures implementation success through a structured set of metrics aligned to each stage of the delivery lifecycle: Kickoff & Discovery, Design–Build–Configure, Testing, Training & Change, Launch & Go-Live, and Hyper-care. These metrics assess readiness, activation, adoption, behavioral alignment, user satisfaction, and early cultural and operational impact, all within the AIRᵉ and ROE frameworks.  Kickoff & Discovery (Readiness Metrics): Success is measured through accurate documentation of requirements, validated data specifications, integration readiness confirmation, completion of change impact assessments, stakeholder alignment, and pre-launch governance setup. Metrics include readiness scores from leadership and managers, completion of communication cascades, and early identification of country-specific needs. These metrics ensure foundational clarity, consistency, and Reinforcement.  Design, Build & Configure (Configuration & Design Quality Metrics): Success is measured through completion of program design decisions, approval of workflows, accurate system configuration, completion of behavioral tagging rules, and integration build milestones. Metrics include configuration acceptance rates, sprint review sign-offs, localization completeness, and policy alignment validation. These indicators demonstrate that Appreciation and Reinforcement are built correctly into the program architecture.  Testing (Quality, Stability & Workflow Integrity Metrics): Success is defined by UAT completion, zero critical-severity issues at go-live, integration accuracy, payroll file alignment, data quality validation, and workflow performance. Metrics include test-case pass rates, defect resolution time, integration health scores, and readiness of all environments. These measures confirm operational reliability and risk-free deployment.  Training & Change (Enablement & Preparedness Metrics): Success is measured through completion of global and local training sessions, learning-module engagement, manager-confidence scores, communication adoption, and readiness assessments across business units. Metrics include percentage of leaders trained, manager training completion, content engagement statistics, employee awareness scores, and BU-level preparedness indicators. These metrics strengthen Authentic Appreciation and support a confident launch.  Launch & Go-Live (Activation & Early Adoption Metrics): Success is defined by first-week activation rates, unique logins, profile completions, first recognition moments, mobile-app adoption, catalog engagement, and stability of support channels. Metrics include early participation rates, recognition frequency, peer vs. manager recognition patterns, and reduction in friction points captured via helpdesk analytics. These show whether employees are embracing the platform quickly and consistently.  Hyper-care (Behavior, Satisfaction & Early Cultural Impact Metrics): Success is measured through AIRᵉ-aligned program health indicators across Appreciation (percentage giving and receiving recognition), Reinforcement (percentage of recognitions tagged to values, distribution of values used, message-quality indicators, badge consistency), Incentivization (budget usage, redemption rates), and Emotional Connect (social engagement, interaction depth, visibility patterns). Additional metrics include CSAT, NPS, ticket-resolution time, sentiment trends, and BU-level adoption curves. Behavioural insights from Recognition Roll and Skillscape show emerging cultural signals.  Across all stages, success is reinforced through milestone completion, governance adherence, integration stability, workflow performance, communication execution, and QBR-driven continuous improvement. This structured approach ensures Wells Fargo achieves not only a successful technical rollout but also the early establishment of consistent, values-aligned recognition habits measured through AIRᵉ and ROE. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal | Can we align this answer to 5.3 ? |  |  | I reworked to have the stages be same as above. | 10.5 | Please describe your proposed implementation plan for the recognition platform. In your response, address:  Reporting: Explain how you will report progress, risks, and outcomes during implementation and after launch. | Vantage Circle provides a structured and transparent reporting model throughout all stages of implementation and post-launch operations. Our approach ensures Wells Fargo receives clear visibility into progress, risks, decisions, dependencies, and emerging outcomes across global and regional workstreams. Reporting is aligned to the six-stage implementation lifecycle—Kickoff & Discovery, Design–Build–Configure, Testing, Training & Change, Launch & Go-Live, and Hyper-care—and is reinforced by AIRᵉ principles to highlight both operational and behavioural readiness.  During Kickoff & Discovery, we establish the full reporting governance model, including cadence, templates, escalation paths, and leadership alignment routines. Weekly status reports provide visibility into overall progress, requirements validation, integration readiness, early risks, and decisions needed. A consolidated RAID log (Risks, Assumptions, Issues, Dependencies) is introduced at the outset and maintained throughout the program to ensure proactive risk management and clear accountability.  During Design–Build–Configure, reporting centres on configuration milestones, sprint progress, integration build status, localisation completion, and policy alignment. Each sprint cycle concludes with a review that documents what was delivered, what remains outstanding, and any emerging risks. Detailed integration dashboards track SSO, HCM, payroll, data feeds, and workflow automation progress. Reports also surface readiness indicators aligned to AIRᵉ, such as value-tag configuration, message-quality prompts, and behavioural nudging mechanisms.  In Testing, we provide daily and weekly testing dashboards to summarize test execution, pass/fail ratios, defect severity trends, integration performance, data quality, and environment stability. UAT reporting includes persona-level readiness, outstanding defects, country-level testing variance, and behavioural workflow accuracy (e.g., correct functioning of Recognition Guide, values tagging, and Profile Badge triggers). Risk reporting intensifies during this stage to ensure any issues are resolved before cutover.  During Training & Change, reporting shifts to adoption readiness. We track training completion, manager and leader participation, communication execution, content engagement, sentiment signals, and BU-level preparedness. Reports highlight whether AIRᵉ elements—Appreciation habits, Reinforcement prompts, and Emotional Connect—are reflected in training participation and early employee feedback.  For Launch & Go-Live, Vantage Circle operates a command-center reporting model. Daily go-live dashboards track platform usage, recognitions sent, logins, mobile adoption, issue trends, response times, integration stability, and catalogue activity. Any risk requiring escalation is communicated through near-real-time updates. Executive summary reports are shared throughout the go-live window.  During Hyper-care, reporting focuses on sustained adoption, support stability, and behavioural traction. Dashboards include recognition participation, early behavioural indicators (values tags, message richness, cross-team recognition), Profile Badge attainment, CSAT and NPS trends, redemption patterns, ticket volume stabilization, and BU/country-level insights. These outputs form the baseline for ongoing Quarterly Business Reviews (QBRs). Post-launch, we continue reporting through structured QBRs and monthly reviews, providing insights on AIRᵉ-aligned KPIs, ROE indicators, country-level adoption trends, manager enablement, and operational health.  This comprehensive reporting approach ensures Wells Fargo has full transparency into program performance, risks, and behavioural outcomes during implementation and beyond, enabling proactive decision-making, stakeholder alignment, and continuous program optimization. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal |  |  |  | I reworked to have same stages as above. |  |  |
| 10.6 | Please describe your proposed implementation plan for the recognition platform. In your response, address:  Case Studies: Share examples of successful implementations for organizations of similar scale, including lessons learned and measurable outcomes. | Our implementation approach for large global enterprises uses the Design, Define, Deliver, Discover and Digest (5D) methodology, supported by a phased rollout model that reduces risk, protects continuity, and accelerates early adoption. For organisations of Wells Fargo’s scale and geographic complexity, we strongly recommend a phased and pilot driven approach similar to our most successful large enterprise implementations.  Phased Implementation Approach Phase 1 • Requirements gathering and workflow mapping • Technical integrations including SSO and HCM (such as Workday) • Configuration of non monetary awards, monetary awards, and greetings • UAT testing and controlled pilot with a subset of users • Enterprise wide launch Phase 2 • Rollout of CSV based (bulk upload) awards • Microsoft Teams integration • Mobile app enablement • UAT and incremental pilot expansion • Full rollout Phase 3 • Configuration of panel based awards and modernised certificate workflows • Long Service Award setup including milestone based celebrations (1, 3, 5, 10, 15 years and beyond) • UAT testing and targeted pilot • Full rollout Phase 4 • Service Yearbook configuration and launch • Retirement Yearbook configuration and launch • UAT and pilot • Enterprise wide rollout This phased model allows Wells Fargo to stabilise foundational capabilities first, gather real usage feedback from pilot cohorts, and introduce advanced features once the core behaviours and workflows are fully adopted.  Case Studies of Large Scale Implementations (Please note: All client references are used with the organization’s consent) We have successfully delivered global, high complexity implementations for organisations of similar scale and operational diversity. Two examples demonstrate our approach.  Case Study 1: Wipro (230,000 Employees Across 60 Countries) Context Wipro required a unified recognition platform to support its Five Habits culture framework, enable global scale, and consolidate disconnected systems used across countries. Approach • Phased rollout across business units, supported by the 5D methodology • Parallel readiness tracks for configuration, training, governance, and communication • Manager capability building through workshops and microlearning • Strong emphasis on values alignment using #tags and structured workflows Outcomes • 553,000 recognitions issued within two years • 768 recognitions per day on average • 97 percent increase in non monetary recognitions • Over 57 percent global coverage • Gold Award at Brandon Hall for Best Advance in Employee Recognition Lesson Learned Early manager enablement and BU specific rollout sequencing are critical in large enterprises. Both reduce friction and accelerate adoption.  Case Study 2: Tata Communications Limited (Global Technology and Telecommunications Organisation) Context The company was undergoing a multi year business transformation and needed a recognition platform that could reinforce new behaviours, connect global teams, and improve cultural cohesion. Approach • Phased delivery starting with core appreciation and non monetary awards • Behavioural reinforcement built through #tags, campaigns, and Profile Badges • BU based sequencing to respect differences in culture and operational maturity • Strong post launch support with structured adoption campaigns Outcomes • Significant increase in cross functional appreciation • Strong behavioural reinforcement among leaders and managers • Recognition became a visible driver of the transformation narrative Lesson Learned Recognition adoption grows faster when behaviour reinforcement mechanisms such as Profile Badges and campaigns are introduced early, rather than waiting until after stabilisation.  Summary Our phased, pilot driven approach ensures predictable delivery, stable adoption, and measurable outcomes across geographically distributed and operationally diverse enterprises. Lessons from comparable implementations demonstrate that sequencing, manager enablement, and early behavioural reinforcement have the greatest impact on long term success. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal | Case Study examples with lessons learnt and measurable outcomes is missing ? | 10.7 | Please describe your approach to driving user adoption and supporting change management for your recognition platform.   Adoption Strategies: What tools, resources, or methodologies do you provide to encourage initial and sustained employee engagement with the platform? | Our adoption strategy follows the Design, Define, Deliver, Discover and Digest methodology, ensuring that employees begin using the platform confidently and continue engaging with it in meaningful, values aligned ways. All adoption activities reinforce AIRᵉ principles across Appreciation, Reinforcement, Incentivization where applicable, and eMotional Connect.  Design and Define: Preparing for Successful Adoption During this stage, our goal is to create clarity, alignment, and excitement before launch. Key activities include: • Tailored rollout planning based on Wells Fargo’s workforce segments such as corporate, branch, contact centre, and operations • Co creation of BU specific communication plans that simplify the shift from current systems • Co branded communication toolkits including email templates, banners, posters, and leader talking points • Onboarding of leaders and Employee Champions to build early advocacy • Values linkage built into launch from day one through the #tag framework This ensures recognition starts off aligned to Wells Fargo’s core values and behavioural expectations.  Deliver: Launch Enablement, Training, and Behaviour Activation This stage focuses on building capability and confidence across the organisation. Tools and resources include: • Live and on demand training for HR, managers, and Employee Champions • Navigation guides, microlearning videos, task based walkthroughs, and FAQs • Manager workshops focused on meaningful, specific, values aligned recognition • Access to Modern Recognition, Ignite, and Elevate to build capability beyond platform navigation • Co branded launch materials to create awareness and excitement • Full use of #tags from the first day of launch so that every recognition reinforces values consistently This ensures recognition begins with the right behaviours embedded.  Discover: Early Engagement and Nudge Based Adoption  In support of early-stage momentum, Wells Fargo will also benefit from Vantage Circle’s Adoption PowerUp Program, a fully sponsored initiative designed to accelerate usage within the first 30-180 days. The program rewards change agents, early adopters, and leaders who model the desired behaviours - such as giving recognition, participating in BU-level campaigns, or encouraging team coverage. PowerUp rules are fully configurable and can be aligned to Wells Fargo’s values, recognising employees or managers based on activity volume, message quality, leadership participation, or BU-level progress. Few suggestive examples include: 1. Top x employees that recognize 3+ unique peers in the first quarter  2. Managers whose teams have a 75% or more recognition coverage in the first quarter  3. Top x Employees that have been recognized for the most varied reasons/ different badges in the first quarter 4. Leaders (VP & above) that have recognized 2+ employees in the first quarter. All and any of these programs will be through csv upload only   This structured, gamified boost helps embed early habits, inspires peer-driven momentum, and ensures that the organisation enters steady-state adoption with strong behavioural foundations.  Adoption tools include:  • Smart nudges and reminders encouraging first recognition and repeat behaviour • Behaviour prompts through the Recognition Guide to improve message quality • Visible social recognition feed that promotes celebration and peer to peer momentum • BU level campaigns to activate groups with lower early adoption • Mobile first pathways that support branch and operations teams This helps establish strong early signals of Appreciation and Reinforcement.  Digest: Sustained Engagement and Behaviour Reinforcement Once the platform stabilises, we reinforce sustained engagement and values alignment. Long term strategies include: • Monthly or quarterly themed campaigns aligned to values, milestones, or global observances • Profile Badges to reward consistency in giving, receiving, and demonstrating values • Continuous values alignment through #tags that remain central to every recognition moment • Spotlight stories that humanise recognition and strengthen Emotional Connect • Skillscape and Recognition Roll for managers to see behaviour patterns and use recognition intelligence in performance and development conversations These tools help recognition become a natural, ongoing habit.  Continuous Monitoring and Optimisation Adoption is supported with structured feedback loops. Support includes: • Quarterly Business Reviews focused on adoption, participation, message quality, and values alignment • Targeted interventions where adoption is low or behaviours need reinforcement • Coaching paths for manager groups • Continuous refinement of communication, campaigns, and workflow design  Summary Through the 5D methodology and AIRᵉ aligned adoption strategies, Vantage Circle provides Wells Fargo with comprehensive tools and resources to drive both initial and long term engagement. With #tags embedded from the start, behavioural reinforcement begins on day one, ensuring recognition is meaningful, values aligned, and culturally consistent across all teams and locations. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal | A big component of this is the PowerUp Adoption Program. Summary Through our 5D model, Vantage Circle provides structured, end to end change management support. | 10.9 | Please describe your approach to driving user adoption and supporting change management for your recognition platform.   Training & Onboarding: What training materials, onboarding programs, or coaching services are available for employees, managers, and administrators? | Vantage Circle provides a comprehensive suite of training, onboarding, and continuous enablement programs designed to ensure successful platform adoption and sustained engagement across all user groups—employees, managers, and administrators. Our approach combines live guidance, on-demand resources, and ongoing learning support to meet diverse organizational and learning needs.  Training and Onboarding Resources Include:  Structured Onboarding Programs: A guided, role-based onboarding journey covering platform navigation, program setup, nomination workflows, and reporting dashboards. Dedicated customer success managers facilitate live walkthroughs during implementation to ensure administrators and program owners are fully equipped before launch.  Live and Interactive Training Sessions: Instructor-led virtual sessions tailored for different user roles, focusing on real-world use cases and best practices. | 10.10 | Please describe your approach to driving user adoption and supporting change management for your recognition platform.   Communication & Promotion: How do you help clients communicate the platform’s benefits, build excitement, and address resistance to change? | Our communication and promotion strategy is integrated throughout the Design, Define, Deliver, Discover and Digest stages of implementation. Our communication strategy will not only promote awareness and adoption of the recognition program but also highlight key behaviors aligned with Wells Fargo’s performance goals, reinforcing a culture of high performance and continuous improvement. The goal is to build awareness, generate excitement, reduce resistance, and reinforce the behaviours encouraged by AIRᵉ.  Design and Define: Setting the Communication Foundation During these stages, we work with Wells Fargo to shape a communication strategy that creates clarity, alignment, and early anticipation. Activities include: • Co creation of a communication plan aligned to Wells Fargo’s culture, tone, and values • Identification of target segments such as corporate, branch, operations, and contact centres • Drafting BU specific versions where tone or context needs localisation • Communication mapping connected to AIRᵉ principles to highlight why recognition matters • Early involvement of Employee Champions and leaders to support readiness • Involvement and briefing of leaders and managers on the goals of the recognition program and their role to model expected behaviors to their teams  • Awareness and excited conveyed in an employee announcement (e.g., video or other modalities) and brief Employee Guide to the recognition program  This ensures early buy in and helps address resistance before launch occurs.  Deliver: Launch Communications and Awareness Building During launch, the focus is on creating high visibility and ensuring all employees understand the purpose and benefits of the platform. Support includes: • Co branded launch toolkits such as email templates, posters, banners, intranet assets, and leader talking points • A structured pre launch and launch calendar with teasers, countdown messages, and platform spotlights • Clear communication of benefits such as ease of use, values alignment through #tags, and the modern recognition experience • Leader and manager driven announcements to reinforce the importance of recognition • Messaging framed around AIRᵉ to build excitement, clarity, and emotional resonance This creates strong awareness and sets a positive tone for adoption.  Discover: Promotion and Behaviour Activation in Early Weeks In the first 30 to 90 days after launch, communication plays a key role in helping employees transition into new habits. Activities include: • Smart in platform notifications to encourage first recognition, message quality, and values linkage • BU targeted nudges and reminders for teams that show lower early adoption • Launch spotlight stories that showcase positive examples of recognition • Weekly or bi weekly communication support depending on launch scale • Manager specific nudges emphasising their role in appreciation and AIRᵉ Reinforcement These early communications help overcome inertia and build new behavioural habits.  Digest: Sustained Communication and Long Term Engagement Once adoption stabilises, we shift to ongoing content and campaigns that reinforce culture and keep engagement high. Our communication cadence includes: • Monthly or quarterly themed campaigns tied to values, global observances, or business milestones • Recognition highlights shared through newsletters, intranet posts, and BU communication channels • Storytelling features such as spotlight posts and success highlights including employee testimonials (e.g., video or brief posts) • Regular refresh of creative assets and visuals to maintain appeal  • Quarterly communication planning with Wells Fargo as part of the QBR process • Additional campaign support available as needed for high impact business events This ensures long term visibility and keeps recognition meaningful and top of mind.  Addressing Resistance to Change Resistance is addressed proactively throughout the communication lifecycle. Approach includes: • Early messaging explaining the why of recognition and its cultural importance • Continuous reinforcement through manager communication and Employee Champions • In platform behavioural prompts that simplify participation • Feedback loops via surveys, helpdesk patterns, and QBR reviews to identify barriers • Adjustments in messaging, tone, or campaign design based on insights This helps ensure the transition feels positive, supported, and culturally aligned.  Summary Communication and promotion efforts begin well before launch and continue throughout the lifecycle of the program. With structured pre launch communications, regular campaign support, in platform nudges, monthly and quarterly engagement initiatives, and continuous feedback loops, Vantage Circle ensures the platform remains visible, valued, and widely adopted across all Wells Fargo teams and locations. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal | Can we add how frequently we provide assistance on communication/ campaigns ? Continuous Improvement: How do you gather user feedback and incorporate it into ongoing platform enhancements or change management strategies? | Our continuous improvement approach is embedded across the Design, Define, Deliver, Discover and Digest stages of our methodology. It ensures that feedback from Wells Fargo’s employees, managers, and administrators flows directly into platform enhancements, configuration optimisation, and change management strategies. Multi Channel Feedback Collection We capture user and administrator input through several structured channels throughout the year. Feedback sources include: • Quarterly client and user surveys to understand sentiment, ease of use, and expectations • In platform feedback prompts where users can share improvement suggestions or flag usability challenges • Customer Success discussions through QBRs and periodic check ins • Feedback from Employee Champions and leaders during adoption reviews • CSAT or quick pulse feedback following major releases or workflow changes • Helpdesk patterns that reveal friction points in navigation or configuration This ensures that insights come from diverse roles and geographies including branch, operations, and corporate teams.  2. Feedback Analysis and Prioritisation Feedback is reviewed collaboratively across Product, REACH and Program Success teams. Our approach includes: • Analysing input alongside adoption data, values linkage patterns, and AIRᵉ insights • Identifying themes across multiple channels to separate isolated requests from systemic needs • Assessing impact on behaviour, usability, scalability, and recognition quality • Prioritising enhancements that strengthen Appreciation, Reinforcement or Emotional Connect • Validating requirements with key stakeholders, especially in large and distributed environments This makes sure that improvements focus on the areas that matter most for sustained engagement.  3. Action, Implementation and Communication Once priorities are set, changes are incorporated into the product roadmap or configuration strategy. Our support includes: • Updating product roadmap cycles to reflect client driven enhancements • Providing release notes, early previews, and briefings to prepare Wells Fargo for upcoming changes • Running additional training, microlearning, or workshops to introduce new features • Supporting internal change management through communication templates, launch kits, and BU level messaging • Monitoring post release adoption to ensure enhancements deliver the expected behavioural impact This ensures changes are understood, adopted, and embedded into day to day behaviour.  4. Reinforcement Through Continuous Improvement Cycles Continuous improvement is not a one time activity. It is woven into long term partnership rhythms. Ongoing reinforcement includes: • QBRs that consolidate feedback, usage insights, AIRᵉ metrics, and behavioural intelligence • Annual program audits for strategic recommendations on design, governance, and manager enablement • Periodic reviews to refine workflows, award categories, and values mapping • Campaign recommendations based on usage and sentiment insights • Opportunities to test new features through controlled pilots This ensures the recognition program remains modern, efficient, and aligned with Wells Fargo’s culture and priorities. For this program we estimate a 6 member team working across shifts and levels of support (L1 & L2) to manage SLA's across timezones. Case Study (Please note: Client reference is used with the organization’s consent).  TATA Communications Tata Communications (10,000+ employees across 190+ countries), where recognition became a core enabler of their transformation from infrastructure-led to platform-led. Through AIRe and ROE, the “Applause” program evolved into a behaviour-shaping engine aligned to DRIVE Ahead transformation behaviours, resulting in stronger alignment to business-critical behaviours, improved collaboration and trust, and significant increases in recognition activity, including a 185% increase in peer-to-peer recognition, 26% rise in managerial awards, 134% increase in active users, and recognition occurring nearly every two minutes.    Our ROE model evaluates impact across four levels,namely Reaction, Learning, Behaviour, and Results using indicators such as recognition fairness, manager capability, values alignment, specificity of recognition messages, leadership reinforcement patterns, collaboration networks, engagement uplift, leadership effectiveness improvements, discretionary effort indicators, and behaviour adoption. Execution KPIs include login rates, % of employees giving and receiving recognition, recognition velocity, message quality, budget utilization, and participation across business units and geographies.    To support ongoing governance, Vantage Circle provides AIRe Assessment Reports, quarterly KPI dashboards, annual recognition audits, global and country-level AIRe reports, GPTW R&R scorecards, case studies, and year-over-year ROE tracking. This enables clients to monitor culture, leadership habits, behavioural adoption, and performance indicators over time. Overall, ROE provides Wells Fargo with a disciplined, evidence-based framework that links recognition to meaningful cultural and performance outcomes, offering a strategic and credible alternative to narrow, purely financial ROI calculations. |  | Account Management / Workday Implementation: Kunal | This needs to align with the Org structure table i pasted in the group |  |  |  |  |  |

| 10.20 | What is your most successful implementation story? Why was it so successful? | Most Successful Implementation Story — Why It Worked Our most successful implementation to date is the enterprise-wide rollout of the global Rewards & Recognition program at Wipro (230,000+ employees across 66 countries). What makes this a standout implementation is not only the outcomes, but the combination of structural, behavioural, and governance decisions that made the program scale effectively in one of the world’s most complex talent environments.  Why This Implementation Was Truly Successful 1. A clear cultural anchor from Day 1 (Five Habits → recognition architecture) The success began with clarity. Wipro knew the behaviours it wanted to strengthen — the Five Habits. We translated these into the platform design through: • Values-linked award categories, • Mapping for behaviour patterns, • Nudges that reinforce those habits, and • Dashboards showing which habits were being lived out. This created a direct line between program design → system behaviour → culture reinforcement. Most recognition programs fail because values sit outside the platform. Wipro succeeded because we built the platform around its culture.  2. The implementation was treated as a behaviour change program, not a tech rollout From the very beginning, the project was positioned as a culture initiative, not an IT enablement activity. This influenced everything: • Leaders were trained on why recognition matters • Managers were trained on how to recognise • Employees were shown what “good recognition” looks like • We structured a drip-feed of behavioural nudges • Early QBRs focused purely on adoption patterns, not feature usage This approach ensured that recognition behaviour shifted quickly and sustainably.  3. Deep co-creation with HR, business leaders, and culture teams The implementation succeeded because it wasn’t done for Wipro but with Wipro. We co-designed: • Award criteria, • Exception workflows, • Approval models for different BUs, • Leadership communication rhythms, • Global vs local recognition norms. This co-creation ensured: • Leaders felt ownership, • HR teams were confident with governance, and • Employees recognised the program as authentically “Wipro,” not a vendor system.  4. Strong governance early on prevented future complexity Wipro is a matrixed organisation. Without governance, recognition programs splinter. We helped establish foundational governance principles early: • Who can configure what, • What approvals are needed, • How values map to awards, • How many award types should exist, • What monthly/quarterly reporting looks like. This ensured consistency across 66 countries without diluting local relevance.  5. Rigorous change management, executed at global scale What made this implementation uniquely successful was the scale and sophistication of the change program: • Phased launches for different geographies, • Multi-format communication campaigns, • Multilingual enablement materials, • Manager workshops, • Microlearning series, • Launch roadshows, • Role-based training for HR partners and business leaders. Wipro didn’t simply "roll out a platform". They deployed a systematic change management engine, with us as their strategic partner.  6. Intelligent iteration using real adoption data (not assumptions) In the first six months, we analysed real usage patterns: • BU-level adoption differences • Peak/low activity cycles • Manager participation • Cross-functional recognition flows • Values demonstrated most frequently These insights helped the PSM team: • Adjust configurations, • Recalibrate award values, • Strengthen specific Habit reinforcements, • Conduct manager interventions, and • Refresh communication strategy. This is why adoption didn’t spike and drop, but kept rising.  7. Sustained reinforcement → measurable culture shift Because the implementation built strong behavioural foundations, Wipro saw: • 553,000+ recognitions • 97.5% growth in peer-led recognitions • 57%+ workforce coverage • 768 recognitions per day • A Brandon Hall Gold Award These outcomes were the direct result of an implementation that aligned people, processes, leadership, and behaviour from the start.  Summary — Why This Story Matters for Wells Fargo This implementation was successful because it brought together: • Cultural alignment, • Deep co-design, • Disciplined governance, • Thoughtful change management, • Manager capability-building, • Behavioural reinforcement, and • Continuous iteration through data. It demonstrates exactly the capability Wells Fargo requires: the ability to implement a global recognition program in a highly distributed, multi-business, multi-country enterprise, and make it work. |  | Program Success Management / References: Atif |  |  |  |  |  |  |

| 10.30 | Describe your platform’s development roadmap as it relates to incorporating learning, best practices, and benchmarking data. In your response, please address: How do you gather and integrate client feedback, industry trends, and emerging best practices into your product development lifecycle? | Vantage Circle’s development roadmap is shaped by a structured and research driven process that integrates client feedback, industry trends, AIRᵉ benchmarking data, and behavioural science. This ensures the platform evolves continuously, aligns with emerging best practices, and delivers meaningful value for large and distributed enterprises.  Client Feedback Integration We gather client insights across multiple channels, including quarterly surveys, in platform feedback prompts, customer success interactions, and structured QBR discussions. These inputs are synthesised by our Product and REACH team. REACH refers to our Research, Education and Advisory Capability Hub. Together they identify recurring needs, friction points, and enhancement opportunities. High impact themes are then translated into roadmap priorities, workflow improvements, and new capability features that directly respond to client requirements.  Industry Trends and Benchmarking Data Our roadmap is informed by extensive research conducted by REACH, including the annual Global AIRᵉ Report, country level studies, and ongoing behavioural research in partnership with academic institutions and HR thought leaders. Insights from more than two thousand AIRᵉ assessments, cross sector benchmarking, and platform wide behavioural analytics help us identify what separates high effectiveness recognition cultures from others. These findings shape roadmap decisions related to nudges, manager guidance, recognition intelligence, and values linked reinforcement.  Integration of Best Practices and Thought Leadership We incorporate principles from organisational psychology, behavioural science, and global HR thought leadership. Expertise from leaders such as Dave Ulrich and Chester Elton influences enhancements focused on message quality, manager capability, habit building mechanisms, and culture reinforcement.  Examples of Roadmap Features Inspired by These Insights Several of our most impactful features were created directly in response to client feedback, research observations, and benchmarking insights: • #Tag Framework: Developed to enable consistency and clear values linkage while still allowing badges to represent emotions, actions, and outcomes. This framework also supports deeper intelligence layers such as Profile Badges, Recognition Roll, and Skillscape. • Boost: Built to simplify manager led spot awards by reducing decision fatigue related to award value selection. Managers give a standard value award and leaders can increase the value with one click based on perceived impact, making recognition simpler and more timely. • Profile Badges: Designed to reinforce behavioural consistency, which AIRᵉ highlights as a core marker of high effectiveness cultures. Values based badges drive cultural alignment while activity based badges increase platform engagement. • Teams and Copilot Integration: Introduced after observing that employees often missed recognition moments while switching between systems. Integrating recognition into Teams and enabling AI assisted prompts helps employees recognise in a timely and effortless manner. • Recognition Guide: Created after research showed that message quality strongly affects felt appreciation. The tool provides AI assisted guidance and scoring to help employees write authentic, meaningful, and values aligned messages. • Skillscape and Recognition Roll (Roadmap): Developed to turn recognition data into behavioural intelligence. These features help leaders see behavioural hotspots, understand capability trends, and use recognition as an input into performance, potential, and development conversations.  Roadmap Governance and Execution Roadmap decisions are prioritised based on behavioural impact, scalability, alignment with global best practices, client adoption patterns, and technical feasibility. Product releases follow structured cycles, with clients receiving advance visibility through release notes, roadmap updates, and enablement materials. Program Success Managers support training, adoption, and change readiness to ensure seamless rollout.  Summary Through continuous integration of client feedback, AIRᵉ benchmarking, behavioural research, and global industry insights, Vantage Circle ensures its platform remains modern, evidence based, and aligned with the evolving needs of enterprise recognition programs. This approach supports ongoing innovation and ensures that Wells Fargo benefits from a platform that strengthens culture, promotes better leadership behaviours, and delivers measurable outcomes over time. |  | Atif/Kunal |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| 10.31 | Describe your platform’s development roadmap as it relates to incorporating learning, best practices, and benchmarking data. In your response, please address: What is your process for identifying, validating, and implementing benchmarking data to enhance platform features and client outcomes? | Our platform's development roadmap is strategically designed to incorporate industry-leading learning, best practices, and benchmarking data to continuously enhance platform capabilities and drive measurable client outcomes.  Process for Identifying and Validating Benchmarking Data  We employ a multi-faceted approach to identify and validate benchmarking data. First, we conduct extensive market research and competitive analysis to understand industry trends, emerging best practices, and peer performance metrics. We partner with leading HR research organizations and analyze aggregated data from our own client base to establish meaningful benchmarks relevant to employee recognition and engagement. This data is rigorously validated through peer review, statistical analysis, and cross-referencing with authoritative sources to ensure accuracy and relevance.  Integration into Platform Features  Once validated, benchmarking data is systematically integrated into our platform features through dedicated analytics dashboards and reporting capabilities. Clients can view their organization's performance against industry standards, peer groups, and global benchmarks, enabling them to identify gaps and opportunities for improvement. The platform automatically surfaces actionable insights based on benchmarking comparisons, helping clients optimize recognition frequency, participation rates, budget allocation, and program design.  Continuous Learning and Enhancement  Our roadmap prioritizes regular updates based on evolving best practices in employee engagement, recognition program effectiveness, and organizational culture. We conduct quarterly reviews of benchmarking data and client outcomes to identify emerging trends, successful strategies, and areas requiring innovation. This intelligence feeds into our product development cycle, ensuring that new features and enhancements reflect the latest evidence-based approaches to recognition and employee engagement.  Through this systematic process, we ensure that our platform remains at the forefront of industry standards, delivering tangible value to clients by aligning their recognition programs with proven best practices and measurable success metrics |  | Solution & Technical Queries: Hemanga |  |  |  |  |  |  |

We follow a structured release schedule that includes quarterly major updates alongside monthly incremental enhancements to ensure the platform remains aligned with emerging trends and client needs.  Update Frequency and Cadence  We conduct comprehensive reviews of benchmarking data, client feedback, and market trends on a quarterly basis. Based on these insights, we identify high-impact improvements and new features for integration into our platform. Major releases typically occur once per quarter, with minor updates and optimization patches released monthly. This balanced approach ensures stability and predictability while maintaining agility in responding to significant market shifts or breakthrough innovations in employee recognition practices.  Client Communication and Transparency  We maintain transparent and proactive communication channels to keep clients informed of all updates and changes. Key communication mechanisms include:  Advance Release Notes: Detailed documentation is provided 2-4 weeks before major releases, outlining new features, enhancements, and any required actions from clients.  Product Roadmap Visibility: Clients have access to our public product roadmap, which provides visibility into planned features, benchmarking initiatives, and strategic direction.  Change Management Sessions: For significant updates, we conduct webinars and training sessions to help clients understand new capabilities and best practices for leveraging updated features.  Dedicated Client Success Teams: Our client success managers proactively reach out to discuss how new updates and benchmarking insights may benefit each organization's specific recognition program objectives.
